Three Types of Scholars' Aspirations in Religion
Ibn Asakir classifies scholars into three types based on their focus on fiqh or usul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's classification of scholars based on their primary focus of study and the legitimizing role of the hadith 'Ikhtilaf ummati rahma' as interpreted by al-Qaffal al-Marwazi.

Core Idea
Scholars' different aspirations serve the community like craftsmen's specializations.

Ibn Asakir presents a nuanced classification of religious scholars, dividing them into those who specialize in fiqh, those who specialize in usul al-din, and those who combine both. He then connects this to the famous hadith about difference being a mercy, quoting al-Qaffal al-Marwazi's interpretation that this refers to difference in aspirations, not doctrine. This lesson explores the classification and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation to get the overall meaning.
Notice the three categories Ibn Asakir presents.
2
Identify the three types
List the three types of scholars mentioned: those focused on fiqh only, those focused on usul only, and those who combine both.
The third type is exemplified by the Ash'aris of Yemen.
3
Examine the hadith interpretation
Focus on the quote from al-Qaffal al-Marwazi. How does he interpret the hadith 'Ikhtilaf ummati rahma'?
He interprets 'ikhtilaf' as difference in aspirations (himam), not in doctrine.
4
Reflect on complementarity
Consider why Ibn Asakir includes the comment that fiqh specialists accept usul positions with minimal proof, and usul specialists follow a fiqh madhhab. What does this say about their relationship?
The passage emphasizes that both specializations are legitimate and beneficial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدين على أضرب منه من قصر همته على التفقه في الدين بدلائله وحججه من التفسير والحديث والإجماع والقياس دون التبحر في دلائل الأصول ومنهم من قصر همته على التبحر في دلائل الأصول دون التبحر في دلائل الفقه ومنهم من جعل همته فيهما جميعا كما فعل الأشعريون من أهل اليمن حيث قالوا لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أتيناك لنتفقه في الدين ولنسألك عن أول هذا الأمر كيف كان وفى ذلك تصديق ما روى عن المصطفى صلى الله عليه وسلم ( اختلاف أمتي رحمة ) كما سمعت من الشيخ الإمام أبي الفتح ناصر بن الحسن العمري قال : سمعت الشيخ الإمام أبا بكر القفال المروزى رحمه الله يقول : معناه اختلاف هممهم رحمة يعني همة واحد تكون في الفقه وهمة آخر تكون في الكلام، كما تختلف همم أصحاب الحرف في حرفهم ليقوم كل واحد منهم مصالح العباد والبلاد ثم كل من جعل همته في معرفة دلائل الفقه لم ينكر في نفسه ما ذهب إليه أهل الأصول منهم بل ذهب في اعتقاد [الذهب؟] مذهبهم بأقل ما دله على صحته من الحجج إلا أنه رأى أن اشتغاله بذلك أنفع وأولى، ومن صرف همته منهم إلى معرفة دلائل الأصول وحججه ذهب في الفروع مذهب أحد الأئمة الذين سميناهم من فقهاء الأمصار إلا أنه رأى أن اشتغاله بذلك عند ظهور البدع أنفع وأحرى
Religion is of types: among them are those who confine their aspiration to gaining deep understanding of religion through its proofs and arguments from tafsir, hadith, consensus, and analogical reasoning, without delving into the proofs of the principles (usul); and among them are those who confine their aspiration to delving into the proofs of the principles without delving into the proofs of fiqh; and among them are those who make their aspiration for both, as the Ash'aris of the people of Yemen did when they said to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'We have come to you to gain deep understanding in religion and to ask you about the beginning of this matter, how it was.' And in that is confirmation of what has been narrated from the Chosen One (peace be upon him): 'The difference of my community is a mercy.' As I heard from the shaykh al-imam Abu al-Fath Nasir ibn al-Hasan al-Amari: he said: I heard the shaykh al-imam Abu Bakr al-Qaffal al-Marwazi (may Allah have mercy on him) say: Its meaning is the difference of their aspirations is a mercy, meaning one aspiration is in fiqh and another aspiration is in kalam, just as the aspirations of craftsmen differ in their craft so that each one of them can fulfill the interests of the servants and the lands. Then, whoever makes his aspiration to know the proofs of fiqh does not deny in himself what the people of usul (among them) have gone to, but rather he follows in belief their school (madhhab) with the least proof that indicates its correctness, except that he sees that his preoccupation with that is more beneficial and more appropriate. And whoever among them directs his aspiration to know the proofs of usul and its arguments follows in the branches (furu') the school of one of the imams we have named from the jurists of the cities, except that he sees that his preoccupation with that at the time of the appearance of innovations is more beneficial and more fitting.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a classification of scholars based on their primary focus of study. Ibn Asakir divides the religious scholars into three groups: those who dedicate themselves to fiqh (jurisprudence) using its sources (tafsir, hadith, ijma, qiyas) without delving into the proofs of usul al-din (theological principles); those who focus on usul al-din without delving into fiqh; and those who combine both, exemplified by the Ash'aris of Yemen. He then links this to the hadith 'Ikhtilaf ummati rahma' (the difference of opinion among my community is a mercy), quoting al-Qaffal al-Marwazi who interprets it as difference in aspirations, not in doctrine. Each scholar has a distinct role in serving the community. Those who specialize in fiqh do not reject the usul scholars' positions; they accept the basic proofs and focus on fiqh as more beneficial for them. Similarly, usul scholars adhere to a fiqh madhhab but prioritize defending the faith against innovations. This passage legitimizes both specializations and highlights the complementary nature of their work.

Key Terms
همة
دلائل الأصول
دلائل الفقه
التفقه
اختفلف أمتي رحمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Focusing on usul al-din is a distraction from fiqh and less valuable.
Correction: The passage shows that both specializations are legitimate and complementary, with usul scholars following a fiqh madhhab but prioritizing usul work especially in times of innovation.

Checkpoint
What does al-Qaffal al-Marwazi interpret the hadith 'Ikhtilaf ummati rahma' to mean?
A) Difference in doctrine is allowed.
B) Difference in aspirations is a mercy.
C) Difference in legal rulings is a mercy.
D) Difference in beliefs is a mercy.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir's classification shows that diversity in scholarly specialization is a mercy from Allah, enabling the community to benefit from both fiqh and usul expertise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What is the primary aspiration of your own religious study? Do you tend to focus more on practical fiqh or on foundational beliefs? How does this shape your contribution to the Muslim community?
?
Have you ever looked down on a scholar or student for studying a subject different from your own (e.g., kalam vs. fiqh)? How does Ibn Asakir's classification and the craftsman analogy challenge your attitude?
?
If you were living at a time when innovations (bid'ah) were widespread, would you feel it more urgent to study usul or fiqh? Why? And how can you support those who specialize in the other field?

Prayer for the Emir and Appeal against Fitna
Ibn Asakir offers a prayer for the emir and urges action against fitna.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ibn Asakir uses prayer to urge political action against innovation and fitna, and the theological role of the ruler.

Core Idea
The ruler's justice and support for Sunnah are essential for defeating innovation.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir concludes his narration with a heartfelt prayer for the emir, blending spiritual supplication with a clear political appeal. He calls upon the ruler to use his authority to suppress innovation and revive the Sunnah, showing that theological struggles often rely on political support. This reveals the interdependence of religious orthodoxy and political power in medieval Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: it opens with a chain of narrators, then shifts into a direct prayer and appeal.
2
Identify the specific requests for the emir
List the things Ibn Asakir asks Allah for the emir: protection, long life, continuation of blessings, increased success to revive Sunnah and suppress innovation. Observe how each request is tied to religious goals.
These are not generic blessings; they are targeted to the ruler's religious role.
3
Understand the 'fitna' and the ruler's role
The passage refers to an incident that lowers the landmarks of religion and raises innovation. Ibn Asakir urges the emir to strive in removing this fitna. Reflect on why the ruler is the one who can fix it.
This fitna is likely the persecution of Ash'aris mentioned in the book.
4
Reflect on the broader lesson
Consider how this prayer demonstrates the political dimension of doctrinal disputes. The ruler's support is seen as crucial for the triumph of Sunnah over innovation.
Ibn Asakir's appeal shows that theological correctness was partly enforced by political authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخبرنا بهاتين الحكايتين أبو القاسم الشحامي أنا أبو بكر البيهقي مثل ما ههنا. ثم رجعنا إلى رواية أبي بكر بن حبيب نسأل الله عز وجل عصمة الأمير واطالة بقائه وإدامة نعمائه وزيادة توفيقه لإحياء السنة بتقريب أهلها من مجلسه وقمع البدعة بتبعيد أهلها من حضرته ليكثر سرور أهل السنة والجماعة من الفريقين جميعا بمكانه وينتشر صالح دعواتهم له في مشارق الأرض ومغاربها بإحسانه ويرغب إلى الله عز وجل ويتضرع إليه في إمتاع المسلمين ببقاء الشيخ العميد وإدامة نعمته وزيادة توفيقه وعصمته فعلى حسن اعتقاده وصحة دينه وقوة يقينه وكمال عقله وكبر محله اعتماد الكافة في استدراك ما وقع من هذه الواقعة التي هي لمعالم الدين خافضة، ولآثار البدع رافعة ومصيبتها إن دامت والعياذ بالله في كل مصر من أمصار المسلمين داخلة، وقلوب أهل السنة والجماعة بها واجفة، وما ذلك على الله بعزيز أن يوفق الشيخ العميد أدام الله تسديده للاجتهاد في إزالة هذه الفتنة والسعي في إطفاء هذه الثائرة موقنا بما يتبعه في دنياه من الثناء الجميل وفي عقباه من الأجر الجزيل قاضيا حق هذه الدولة العالية التي جعل الله تدبيرها إلى وزمامها بيديه فبقاء الملك بالعدل وصلاحه بصلاح الدين وحلاوته بما يتبعه من الثناء الجميل والله يوفقه ويسدده وعن المكاره يقيه ويحفظه والسلام عليه ورحمة الله وبركاته
And we were told these two stories by Abu al-Qasim al-Shihami, from Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi, similar to what is here. Then we returned to the narration of Abu Bakr ibn Habib: We ask Allah Almighty for the protection of the emir, prolongation of his life, continuation of His blessings upon him, and increase of His success for reviving the Sunnah by bringing its people close to his assembly, and suppressing innovation by distancing its people from his presence, so that the joy of the people of the Sunnah and the community from both groups may increase by his presence, and their righteous supplications for him may spread in the east and west of the earth by his goodness. And he desires from Allah Almighty and beseeches Him to let the Muslims enjoy the life of the shaykh al-amide, and the continuation of His grace, increase of His success and protection. So upon the goodness of his belief, soundness of his religion, strength of his certainty, perfection of his intellect, and greatness of his status, all rely on correcting what has occurred of this incident which is lowering the landmarks of religion and raising the traces of innovation. And if it continues, may Allah protect us, it will enter every city of the Muslims, and the hearts of the people of the Sunnah and the community will be trembling with it. And that is not difficult for Allah to grant success to the shaykh al-amide, may Allah perpetuate his right guidance, to strive in removing this fitna and hastening to extinguish this flame, certain of what follows in his worldly life of good praise and in his afterlife of great reward, fulfilling the right of this high state which Allah made its management with him and its reins in his hands. For the survival of kingship is through justice, and its rectification is through the rectification of religion, and its sweetness is through the good praise that follows. And Allah grants him success and guides him, and protects him from detestable things and preserves him. And peace be upon him and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a lengthy prayer directed to Allah on behalf of the emir (ruler), pleading for his protection, long life, and guidance. The author expresses that the survival of the Sunnah and suppression of innovation depend on the emir. The 'vista' (incident) refers to the persecution of Ash'aris described later. The author urges the emir to fix this situation, promising that his efforts will bring him praise in this world and reward in the hereafter. It emphasizes the role of the ruler in upholding religious orthodoxy.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The prayer is merely a rhetorical formula, not a real plea with consequences.
Correction: Ibn Asakir genuinely calls on the emir's authority to end the fitna, showing that theological disputes were settled by rulers. The prayer's force reflects real power dynamics.

Checkpoint
What does the author ask Allah for on behalf of the emir?
A) Wealth and victory.

C) Victory over enemies.
D) Wisdom in ruling.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir’s prayer shows that reviving Sunnah and suppressing innovation depends on the ruler’s support and just action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Ibn Asakir says 'the survival of kingship is through justice.' For you, what is your 'kingship'—your family, your circle, your self-governance? How does your personal justice (or lack thereof) affect the survival of your faith? What is one unjust habit you will repent from today?

Al-Juwayni on Ijtihad in Usul and Furu'
Al-Juwayni states the principle of ijtihad and al-Ash'ari's view of taswib in furu'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Juwayni's distinction between usul and furu' regarding ijtihad and al-Ash'ari's position that all mujtahids in furu' are correct.

Core Idea
In fundamentals, only one opinion is correct; in branches, all mujtahids may be correct.

In defending al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy, al-Juwayni clarifies a key principle of ijtihad. He distinguishes between the unchangeable fundamentals of religion, where only one view is correct, and the branches where multiple valid interpretations can coexist. This passage presents al-Ash'ari's taswib al-mujtahidin doctrine and shows its compatibility with Shafi'i's school.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp al-Juwayni's precise wording.
2
Identify the ijtihad principle
Note the distinction between usul and furu' and what is obligatory in each.
3
Understand taswib al-mujtahidin
Recognize that al-Ash'ari holds all mujtahids in furu' are correct, and see how al-Juwayni justifies this disagreement with Shafi'i.
4
Consider the example of la sighata lil-amr
Reflect on why this view contradicts Shafi'i's usul and what it implies about al-Ash'ari's methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر الشيخ الامام ركن الدين أبو محمد عبد الله بن يوسف الجويني رحمه الله في آخر كتاب صنفه وسماه عقيدة أصحاب الامام المطلبي الشافعي رضي الله عنه وكافة أهل السنة والجماعة وقال : ونعتقد ان المصيب من اجتهدين في الأصول والفروع واحد ويجب التعيين في الأصول فأما في الفروع فربما يتأتى التعيين وربما لايتأتى ومذهب الشيخ أبي الحسن رحمه تصويب المجتهدين في الفروع وليس ذلك مذهب الشافعي رضي الله عنه وأبو الحسن احد أصحاب الشافعى رضى الله عنهم، فإذا خالفه في شيء ا عرضنا عنه فيه ومن هذا القبيل قوله ان لاصيغة للأمر وتقل وتعز مخالفته أصول الشافعى رضى الله عنه، ونصوصه وربما نسب المبتدعون إليه أنه يقول لبس فى المصحف قرآن ولا في القبر نبي، وكذلك الاستثناء في الإيمان ونفى قدرة الخلق فى الأزل وتكفير العوام وايجاب علم الدليل عليهم وقد تصفحت ما تصفحت من كتبه وتأملت نصوصه في هذه المسائل فوجدتها كلها خلاف ما نسب إليه ولا عجب ان اعترضوا عليه واخترصوا فإنه رحمه فاضح القدرية وعامة المبتدعة وكاشف عوراتهم ولا خير فيمن لا يعرف الله حاسده
And the Shaykh Imam Rukn al-Din Abu Muhammad 'Abd Allah ibn Yusuf al-Juwayni (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned at the end of a book he authored, which he named 'The Creed of the Followers of Imam al-Mutallibi al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) and all Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah,' and said: 'We believe that the correct one among those who exert ijtihad in the usul (fundamentals) and furu' (branches) is one, and specification is obligatory in the usul. As for the furu', sometimes specification is possible and sometimes not. The madhhab of Shaykh Abu al-Hasan (may Allah have mercy on him) is that all mujtahids in the furu' are correct. This is not the madhhab of al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him). Abu al-Hasan is one of the companions of al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with them all). So if he disagrees with him in something, we leave him concerning it. Among such matters is his statement that there is no specific form for the command (la sighata lil-amr), which is [؟] and [؟] in its opposition to the usul of al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) and his texts. And the innovators sometimes attribute to him that he says there is no Qur'an in the mushaf and no prophet in the grave, similarly istithna' (exception) in faith, negation of the power of creation in pre-eternity, takfir of the common people, and making knowledge of the proof obligatory upon them. I have examined as much as I have examined of his books and pondered his texts on these issues, and I found them all contrary to what is attributed to him. It is not surprising that they objected to him and [؟] (invented lies), for he (may Allah have mercy on him) exposed the Qadariyya and all the innovators and uncovered their shame. There is no good in one who does not know Allah's envier.'
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a defense of al-Ash'ari by Imam al-Juwayni, cited from his book 'Creed of the Followers of Imam al-Shafi'i'. Al-Juwayni begins by stating a principle of ijtihad: in the fundamentals (usul) of religion, the correct position is one and must be determined, but in the branches (furu') of fiqh, it may or may not be possible to determine the correct view. He then explains that al-Ash'ari's madhhab is that all mujtahids in the furu' are correct (taswib al-mujtahidin), which differs from al-Shafi'i's view. Since al-Ash'ari is a companion of al-Shafi'i, when he disagrees, al-Juwayni says 'we leave him concerning it.' He gives an example: al-Ash'ari's view that 'there is no specific form for the command' (la sighata lil-amr), which contradicts Shafi'i's usul. Then al-Juwayni lists slanders that innovators attribute to al-Ash'ari, such as denying that the mushaf contains the Qur'an, denying the prophet's presence in his grave, making istithna' in faith, negating the power of creation in pre-eternity, declaring common people disbelievers, and obligating knowledge of proofs upon them. Al-Juwayni declares that after examining al-Ash'ari's books, he found all these accusations false. He concludes by stating that it is no surprise his enemies attacked and invented lies, because al-Ash'ari exposed the Qadariyya and all innovators. This passage defends al-Ash'ari's orthodoxy and shows that his positions were misrepresented.

Key Terms
اجتهاد
أصول
فروع
تصويب المجتهدين
لا صيغة للأمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that al-Ash'ari believed all mujtahids are correct in both usul and furu'.
Correction: Al-Juwayni clarifies that only in furu' are all mujtahids correct; in usul, only one is correct and must be identified.

Checkpoint
According to al-Juwayni, what is the ruling on ijtihad in the usul (fundamentals)?
A) All mujtahids are correct.
B) Only one mujtahid is correct and must be identified.
C) Ijtihad is not allowed in usul.
D) The correct view is unknown.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari held that all mujtahids in furu' are correct, but in usul only one view is right; his disagreement with al-Shafi'i on la sighata demonstrated his independence without leaving Ahl al-Sunna.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe that in matters of usul (fundamentals) only one view is correct. Are you actively seeking that correct view through rigorous study, or have you settled for a comfortable position without verifying it against the evidence from the Qur'an and Sunnah? What step will you take today to move closer to the truth in one foundational belief?
?
The lesson shows that al-Ash'ari and al-Shafi'i disagreed on a furu' matter yet both remained within Ahl al-Sunna. Is there a person you have dismissed or judged harshly because they held a different opinion on a secondary issue? Will you humble yourself and reconsider your attitude towards them as a brother or sister in faith?
?
Al-Juwayni states that in furu', specification may or may not be possible. This implies humility in our judgments about differences. When you encounter a disagreement among scholars on a practical matter, do you assume that only one side is right and the others are wrong, or do you leave room for the possibility that all may be correct? How can you cultivate that tolerance in your heart?

Al-Juwayni Refutes Slanders against Al-Ash'ari
Al-Juwayni lists false accusations against al-Ash'ari and refutes them by citing his own writings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the false accusations leveled against al-Ash'ari and al-Juwayni's refutation based on examining his actual writings.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's works prove he is innocent of the heresies his enemies attribute to him.

After establishing the principle of ijtihad, al-Juwayni turns to defend al-Ash'ari from a series of slanders that were circulating among innovators. These include claims about the Qur'an, the Prophet, faith, and takfir. Al-Juwayni states he personally examined al-Ash'ari's books and found all accusations false. This passage shows how careful scholarship can refute polemical misrepresentations.

Guided Path
1
List the slanders
Read the passage and identify all the false beliefs attributed to al-Ash'ari.
2
Understand each slander
Briefly explain what each accusation means (e.g., 'no Qur'an in mushaf' suggests denial of the written Qur'an as revelation).
3
Al-Juwayni's method of refutation
Notice that al-Juwayni appeals to direct examination of al-Ash'ari's own texts, not just emotional defense.
4
Reflect on the motivation of the slanderers
Al-Juwayni says al-Ash'ari exposed the Qadariyya and innovators, so they attacked him out of animosity.

Al-Ash'ari's own writings, as verified by al-Juwayni, completely exonerate him from the slanders of his opponents, who attacked him because he exposed their falsehood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been misrepresented or slandered because you spoke the truth? Reflect on a time when you stood up for what is right and were attacked in return. What did that reveal about your character and your reliance on Allah? Are you willing to endure slander for the sake of truth, as al-Ash'ari did?
?
Al-Juwayni did not accept the rumors about al-Ash'ari; he went to his books and verified for himself. When you hear a negative claim about a scholar, a teacher, or even a fellow Muslim, do you rush to judge or do you seek evidence from their own words or actions? What would change in your life if you committed to verifying before accepting?
?
The passage ends with a severe warning: 'There is no good in one who does not know Allah's envier.' Who in your life might be envious of your faith or your efforts in Allah's path? Have you ever felt envy towards someone who exposed your faults? How can you purge envy from your heart and instead become grateful for those who help you see the truth?

Al-Ash'ari's Fiqh Madhhab: Shafi'i, Not Maliki
Ibn Asakir concludes that al-Ash'ari was Shafi'i and addresses a Maliki attribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ibn Asakir provides evidence that al-Ash'ari followed the Shafi'i school and addresses a claim of Maliki affiliation.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari was a Shafi'i in fiqh, as confirmed by his own supporters and even Maliki scholars.

In this concluding passage, Ibn Asakir summarizes the evidence for al-Ash'ari's Shafi'i affiliation. He references multiple authorities, including Ibn Furak, and then addresses a problematic phrase attributed to al-Ash'ari that might suggest Maliki leanings. Ibn Asakir shows that Maliki commentators themselves dismiss that phrase as forged or precautionary, reinforcing the Shafi'i attribution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation to get the flow of Ibn Asakir's argument.
Notice the footnote marker and how it interrupts the sentence.
2
Identify the claim and evidence
Find where Ibn Asakir states that al-Ash'ari followed the Shafi'i school and what evidence he provides (the story, Ibn Furak, other scholars).
He uses the word 'دلالة' (indication) to connect the story to the Shafi'i affiliation.
3
Analyze the refutation
Examine how Ibn Asakir addresses the potential objection from a treatise attributed to al-Ash'ari that seems Maliki. Note the two possibilities: forged or precautionary (ihtiras).
He cites Maliki commentators as agreeing with this refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الامام الحافظ رضی الله عنه وفي هذه الحكاية دلالة للذكى الالمعي أن ابا الحسن كان يذهب مذهب الشافعي وكذلك ذكر أبو بكر بن فورك الأصبهاني في كتاب طبقات المتكلمين و ذكره غيره من أئمتنا وشيوخنا الماضين، ، فكفى أبا الحسن فضلا ان يشهد (1) ينسب إليه في رسالته في مذهب مالك لفظة يتسارع إلى نقلها شيوخ منهم انه على معتقدهم مع ان شراحها من أئمة المالكية مطبقون على أنها اما مدسوسة أو من قبيل الاحتراس بالرفع أى المجيد بذاته لا بالخدم والخول راجع ابن الفاكهاني والابي، وأهل مذهب الرجل أعلم بمذهبه.
The imam, the hafiz, may Allah be pleased with him, said: In this story there is an indication for the intelligent that Abu al-Hasan followed the school of al-Shafi'i. Likewise, Abu Bakr ibn Furak al-Isbahani mentioned it in his book 'Tabaqat al-Mutakallimin', and others of our imams and past shaykhs mentioned it. So it suffices as a virtue for Abu al-Hasan that... (1) It is attributed to him in his treatise on the school of Malik a word that some shaykhs hasten to transmit, saying that he was upon their creed, while its commentators from the Malikiyya imams are unanimous that it is either forged or of the type of precaution by raising (i.e., 'al-Majid bi-dhatihi' not by servants and retainers). See Ibn al-Fakahani and al-Abi. And the people of a man's school are more knowledgeable about his school.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is the author's (Ibn Asakir's) analysis of the preceding anecdote. He states that the story provides evidence that al-Ash'ari followed the Shafi'i madhhab, a point also recorded by al-Bayhaqi and others. He then addresses a potential objection: a word in a treatise attributed to al-Ash'ari in defense of the Maliki school might suggest he was Maliki. However, the author clarifies that the Maliki commentators themselves consider that word to be either a forgery or a form of rhetorical precaution (al-ihtiras) meaning something like 'the Majid by His essence, not by servants and retainers.' He references Ibn al-Fakahani and al-Abi, and concludes that the people of a man's own school are most knowledgeable about his school.

Key Terms
مذهب الشافعي
أبو بكر بن فورك
طبقات المتكلمين
احتراس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Ash'ari was a Maliki in fiqh because of a phrase in his treatise.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that Maliki scholars themselves reject that phrase as forged or precautionary, and multiple sources confirm he was Shafi'i.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, which madhhab did al-Ash'ari follow in fiqh?
A) Maliki
B) Shafi'i
C) Hanafi
D) Hanbali

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir concludes that al-Ash'ari was a Shafi'i, and any Maliki attribution is based on a dubious phrase dismissed by Maliki authorities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a claim about a scholar's position, do you rush to accept it if it matches your expectations—or do you seek verification from the scholar's own followers, as the Maliki commentators were consulted here? What would it take for you to pause and investigate like Ibn Asakir?
?
The shaykhs hastened to transmit a phrase without verifying it. In your own learning, are there phrases or ideas you have accepted without checking their source or context? Which one comes to mind, and will you commit to tracing it back today?
?
The passage shows that even a single forged word can spread confusion for centuries. Who might be misled by your own words if you speak without knowledge? Will you answer for that on the Day of Judgment? How will you ensure your speech about scholars is accurate?

Ruling on Books of Philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima
Qadi al-'Askar reports the ruling on books of philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the ruling of early Sunni scholars regarding books of philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima, and the reasons for prohibiting their study and possession.

Core Idea
Falsehood disguised as tawhid is more dangerous than open disbelief.

This lesson presents a report from a prominent Hanafi scholar, Qadi al-'Askar, who examined early books on tawhid. He found that many were written by philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima, filled with shirk and hypocrisy yet misleadingly titled as tawhid. The early scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah unanimously avoided such books to protect the faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a feel for its flow, then read the English translation. Notice that it is a report from a specific scholar.
Qadi al-'Askar is a known Hanafi authority.
2
Identify the three categories of forbidden books
The passage mentions three groups: philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima. For each group, specific names are given. Note the names and the general description.
The philosophers include Ishaq al-Kindi and al-Isfarazi; Mu'tazila include 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi, al-Jubba'i, al-Ka'bi, al-Nazzam; Mujassima include Muhammad ibn al-Haysam.
3
Understand the reasons for prohibition
For each group, extract the reason given why their books cannot be kept or studied. For philosophers: filled with shirk and hypocrisy. For Mu'tazila: cause doubts and weaken belief. For Mujassima: they are the worst of innovators.
The common thread: these books present falsehood under the guise of tawhid.
4
Reflect on scholarly practice
Notice that the early scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah did not keep these books. Ask yourself what principle this upholds about protecting the creed.
This shows that preventing harm to faith takes priority over academic curiosity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر أبو العباس المعروف بقاضى العسكر، وكان من كبراء أصحاب أبي حنيفة رضى الله عنه انه نظر فى كتب صنفها المتقدمون في علم التوحيد، قال فوجدت بعضها للفلاسفة مثل إسحق الكندي والاسفرازي وأمثالهما وذلك كله خارج عن الطريق المستقيم زائغ عن الدين القويم لا يجوز النظر فى تلك الكتب لانه يجر إلى المهالك لأنها مملؤة من الشرك والنفاق، مسماة باسم التوحيد، ولهذا ما امسك المتقدمون من أهل السنة والجماعة شيئا من كتبهم ووجدت تصانيف كثيرة في هذا الفن من العلم للمعتزلة مثل عبد الجبار الرازي والجبائي والكعبي والنظام وغيرهم، ولا يجوز امساك تلك الكتب ولا النظر فيها كيلا تحدث الشكوك ويوهن الاعتقاد ولئلا ينسب ممسكها إلى البدعة ولهذا ما امسكها المتقدمون من أهل السنة والجماعة فكذا المجسمة صنفوا كتبا في هذا الفن مثل محمد بن الهيصم وامثاله ولا يحل النظر فيها ولا امساكها فإنهم شر أهل البدع، وقد وقع في يدى بعض هذه التصانيف فما أمسكت منها شئيا
And Abu al-Abbas, known as Qadi al-'Askar, who was among the great companions of Abu Hanifa (may Allah be pleased with him), mentioned that he examined books authored by the early scholars on the science of tawhid. He said: I found some of them for the philosophers, such as Ishaq al-Kindi and al-Isfarazi and their like, and all of that is outside the straight path, deviating from the upright religion. It is not permissible to look into those books, because it leads to destruction, for they are filled with shirk and hypocrisy, named with the name of tawhid. For this reason, the early scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah did not keep any of their books. And I found many writings in this field of knowledge for the Mu'tazila, such as 'Abd al-Jabbar al-Razi, al-Jubba'i, al-Ka'bi, al-Nazzam, and others. It is not permissible to keep those books nor to look into them, so that doubts do not arise and belief is not weakened, and so that the one who keeps them is not attributed to innovation. For this reason, the early scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah did not keep them. Likewise, the Mujassima authored books in this field, such as Muhammad ibn al-Haysam and his likes. It is not permissible to look into them nor to keep them, for they are the worst of the people of innovation. Some of these writings came into my hand, and I did not keep any of them.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage reports the stance of Abu al-Abbas Qadi al-'Askar, a prominent Hanafi scholar, regarding books on tawhid. He states that books by philosophers (e.g., al-Kindi, al-Isfarazi) are outside the straight path and filled with shirk, yet misleadingly titled as tawhid. Early Ahl al-Sunnah did not keep them. Similarly, books by the Mu'tazila (listed by name) and the Mujassima (anthropomorphists) are forbidden because they generate doubts, weaken faith, and associating with them may lead to accusations of innovation. The author himself confirms that he did not keep any such books when they came into his hands.

Key Terms
التوحيد
الفلاسفة
المعتزلة
المجسمة
البدعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The prohibition applies to all books on kalam or theology.
Correction: The prohibition is specifically against books that promote falsehood under the guise of tawhid, not against all theological works.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, why are books of the Mu'tazila forbidden?
A) They contain grammatical errors.
B) They cause doubts and weaken belief.
C) They are too difficult to understand.
D) They were written by disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Early Sunni scholars prohibited keeping or studying books by philosophers, Mu'tazila, and Mujassima because they disguise falsehood as tawhid and weaken belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek knowledge, are you willing to discard a book or a lecture that you find attractive if it comes from a source that deviates from the methodology of Ahl al-Sunnah? What is keeping you from doing so?
?
Qadi al-'Askar did not keep any of those books, even though they came into his hand. Is there any piece of knowledge, a YouTube clip, or a book that you hold onto despite knowing it contains deviant ideas? What would it cost your faith to let it go?
?
The early scholars protected their hearts by avoiding books that disguise shirk as tawhid. What disguised falsehoods have you allowed into your heart because they came wrapped in religious language? Will you commit to removing them today?

Defense of Al-Ash'ari Against Takfir, Tadlil, and Tabdi'
Imam Ibn Asakir argues that disagreements over al-Ash'ari do not warrant takfir, tadlil, or tabdi'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Ibn Asakir argues that disagreements over al-Ash'ari do not warrant accusations of major error.

Core Idea
Scholarly disagreement does not justify takfir or tabdi'.

Imam Ibn Asakir addresses a crucial principle in Islamic theology: how to treat scholarly disagreements. In this passage, he defends Imam al-Ash'ari against harsh accusations, explaining that the issues in question are not fundamental differences. He draws on the example of the great imams to normalize respectful disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Note the key terms: takfir, tadlil, tabdi'.
The passage is a single flowing argument.
2
Identify the three accusations
The imam says the issues do not necessitate takfir, tadlil, or tabdi'. Understand what each term means: declaring disbelief, declaring misguidance, declaring innovation.
3
Examine the reasoning
Notice the claim that if the matter were investigated, the disagreement would be seen as agreement. This is a key point: the differences are not fundamental.
The imam normalizes scholarly difference by citing Abu Hanifa's companions.
4
Reflect on the example of Abu Hanifa
The two companions of Abu Hanifa (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagreed with him on many issues. Yet they are respected scholars. This shows that disagreement does not imply error.
The passage ends with a prayer for all scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الامام الحافظ رضى الله عنه وهذه المسائل التي أشار إليها لا تكسب أبا الحسن تشنيعا ولا توجب له تكفيرا ولا تضليلا ولا تبديعا، ولو حققوا الكلام فيها لحصل الاتفاق وبان بأن الخلاف فيها حاصله الوفاق، ومازال العلماء يخالف بعضهم بعضا ويقصد دفع قول خصمه إبراما ونقضا ويجتهد في إظهاره خلافه بحثا وفحصا، ولا يعتقد ذلك في حقه عيبا ونقصا وقديما ما خالف ابا حنيفة صاحباه وأجابا في كثير من المسائل بما اباه والله يتغمد جميع العلماء برحمته ويحشرنا في زمرتهم بلطفه .ورأفته
The Imam, the Hafiz (may Allah be pleased with him) said: These issues that he referred to do not earn Abu al-Hasan disrepute, nor do they necessitate his takfir, tadlil, or tabdi'. If they had investigated the matter, agreement would have been reached, and it would have become clear that the disagreement in them essentially amounts to agreement. The scholars have always differed with one another, aiming to refute and rebut their opponent's statement, and striving to show their contrary view through investigation and examination, without considering that to be a defect or deficiency in him. And long ago, Abu Hanifa's two companions differed with him and answered many issues with what he rejected. And Allah envelopes all scholars with His mercy, and may He gather us among their group by His kindness and clemency.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage is the imam's response to those who criticized al-Ash'ari on specific issues. The imam argues that these minor disagreements should not lead to takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever), tadlil (declaring someone misguided), or tabdi' (declaring someone an innovator). He explains that if the issues were properly studied, it would be seen that the disagreements are actually points of agreement. He normalizes scholarly difference by noting that even Abu Hanifa's two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagreed with him on many issues. The passage ends with a prayer for all scholars to be covered by Allah's mercy.

Key Terms
التكفير
التضليل
التبديع
الخلاف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any disagreement justifies takfir or tabdi'.
Correction: The imam argues that when the difference is not fundamental, it should not lead to such extreme judgments.

Checkpoint
According to the imam, why should the issues where al-Ash'ari is criticized not lead to takfir?
A) Because he repented.
B) Because the disagreement is essentially one of wording and agreement is possible.
C) Because he was a scholar of hadith.
D) Because he was a follower of a particular madhhab.

Key Takeaway
Disagreement among scholars on non-fundamental issues does not warrant accusations of disbelief or innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever condemned another Muslim in your heart or out loud for a view they held that you disagreed with? Recall that moment: did you first investigate the matter as thoroughly as Ibn Asakir advises, or did you jump to judgment? What would it take to ask forgiveness or change your attitude?
?
The passage shows that even the closest students of Abu Hanifa disagreed with him on many issues without considering him deficient. Is there a scholar, teacher, or fellow Muslim you have distanced yourself from because of disagreement? Can you, right now, pray for them as Ibn Asakir prays for all scholars to be covered by mercy?
?
If you were in a situation where a respected scholar like al-Ash'ari was being accused of innovation based on a few issues, would you hold back your tongue or join the criticism? Your answer reveals whether you have internalized this lesson's call for caution and mercy. What specific step will you take today to decrease your rush to condemn and increase your pursuit of understanding?

Hadith on the Head of One Hundred Years
Ibn Asakir narrates the hadith on the head of 100 years as proof for qarn length.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) establishes the duration of a century (qarn) as one hundred years.

Core Idea
A century is one hundred years, confirmed by the Prophet's own words.

This lesson presents a key hadith that Ibn Asakir uses to define the length of a century. The Prophet ﷺ declared that after one hundred years from that night, no one from that generation would remain. This hadith is agreed upon for its authenticity. Let's examine its chain and meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith with its chain
Start by reading the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the full chain of narrators from Ibn Asakir back to Abdullah ibn Umar. This chain ensures the hadith is authentic.
2
Understand the Prophet's statement
The Prophet said that at the head of one hundred years from that night, none of those on earth would remain. This means the entire generation would pass away within that century.
The phrase 'head of one hundred years' refers to the beginning of the hundred-year period.
3
Connect to the definition of 'qarn'
Ibn Asakir uses this hadith to prove that a 'qarn' (century/generation) is 100 years. The hadith shows that the generation ends after 100 years.
The word 'qarn' is often translated as 'century' or 'generation'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و يدل على مبلغ قدر القرن وامده مما لايتمارى أحد في صحة سنده ما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو المظفر عبد المنعم ابن الاستاذ أبي القسم عبد الكريم بن هوازن القشيري بنيسابور قال انا أبي رحمه الله قال انا أبو نعيم عبد الملك بن الحسن بن محمد الأزهرى قال انا أبو عوانة يعقوب ابن اسحق بن ابراهيم بن الاسفرايني قال ثنا السلمي يعني أحمد بن يوسف قال ثنا عبد الرزاق قال انا معمر عن الزهري عن سالم وأبى بكر بن سليمان يعني ابن أبي خيثمة ان عبدالله بن عمر قال صلى بنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ذات ليلة صلاة العشاء في آخر حياته فلما سلم قال أرأيتم ليلتكم هذه فإن على رأس مائة سنة منها لا يبقى ممن على ظهر الأرض أحد ) يريد بذلك ان ينخرم ذلك القرن فلا يبقى احد متفق على صحته رواه مسلم عن محمد بن رافع وعبد بن حميد عن عبدالرزاق
And it indicates the extent of the status of the century and its duration, concerning which no one doubts the correctness of its chain, what we were informed by Shaykh Abu al-Muzaffar Abd al-Mun'im ibn al-Ustadh Abi al-Qasim Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin al-Qushayri in Nishapur, he said: my father narrated to us, may Allah have mercy on him, he said: Abu Nu'aym Abd al-Malik ibn al-Hasan ibn Muhammad al-Azhari narrated to us, he said: Abu Awana Ya'qub ibn Ishaq ibn Ibrahim ibn al-Isfara'ini narrated to us, he said: al-Sulami, meaning Ahmad ibn Yusuf, narrated to us, he said: Abd al-Razzaq narrated to us, he said: Ma'mar narrated to us from al-Zuhri from Salim and Abu Bakr ibn Sulayman, meaning Ibn Abi Khaythama, that Abdullah ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ led us in prayer one night, the night prayer, at the end of his life. When he said the salam, he said: 'Do you see this night of yours? For at the head of one hundred years from it, none of those on the face of the earth will remain.' He intended by that that that century would break off so that no one would remain. It is agreed upon its authenticity. Muslim narrated it from Muhammad ibn Rafi' and Abd ibn Hamid from Abd al-Razzaq.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage provides a hadith with a full chain of transmission to support the definition of a 'qarn' (century/generation) as one hundred years. The hadith is from Abdullah ibn Umar, reporting that the Prophet said that after one hundred years from that night, no one on earth would remain from that generation. Ibn Asakir interprets this as meaning the century 'breaks off' (yankharim) with no one left. He notes that the hadith is agreed upon as authentic and was narrated by Muslim.

Key Terms
رأس مائة سنة
ينخرم
القرن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the hadith means everyone dies exactly at 100 years from that night, but it refers to the end of the entire generation.
Correction: The Prophet said 'from those on the face of the earth' meaning the people alive at that time, not every person everywhere. After 100 years, that generation would have passed away.

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet say about the head of one hundred years?
A) That no one on earth from that generation will remain.
B) That a new century will begin.
C) That people will become better.
D) That knowledge will increase.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's statement about the head of one hundred years provides the authoritative definition of a century (qarn) as a period of one hundred years in Islamic tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet ﷺ said that after one hundred years, none of that generation would remain. You are part of this generation. What actions are you taking today that will outlast you? Write down one concrete change you will make this week to leave a lasting legacy of faith.
?
Ibn Asakir relied on an authentic hadith to define a fundamental term. Do you verify the sources of your religious knowledge, or do you accept things without question? Commit to checking the source of one Islamic teaching you believe today.
?
This hadith reminds us that entire generations come and go. Where is your attachment to this world preventing you from preparing for the next? Name one worldly attachment you need to release and take a step toward letting it go.

The Hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr on the Length of a Qarn
Ibn Asakir narrates the hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr confirming qarn is 100 years.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the hadith of Abdullah ibn Busr provides direct evidence that a qarn equals 100 years, and how the narrative confirms this.

Core Idea
A qarn is exactly 100 years, as confirmed by the Prophet's own words.

In this passage, Ibn Asakir presents a hadith that directly answers the question of how long a qarn is. Through a detailed chain of narration, we learn the story of Abdullah ibn Busr, who was told he would live a qarn, and the Prophet explicitly defined it as 100 years. This narrative not only provides the definition but also shows its fulfillment in Abdullah's lifespan.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the sense of the narrative. Then read the English translation carefully, noting the chain of narration and the key dialogue.
This hadith is a direct textual evidence for the definition of qarn.
2
Identify the key elements
Look for the chain of transmission, the prophecy about living a qarn, Abdullah's question about its length, the Prophet's answer, and the fulfillment in Abdullah's age.
The hadith explicitly gives the number: 100 years.
3
Understand the significance
This hadith is a clear proof from the Sunnah that a qarn is 100 years. It also shows the reliability of prophetic traditions as the event was fulfilled exactly.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some might think the child only lived 95 years, but the hadith clarifies he lived 100 years total. This shows the importance of reading the full account.
The misconception is addressed in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدل عليه أيضا ما أخبرنا الشيخ أبو الفتح يوسف بن عبد الواحد بن محمد بن يوسف الماهانى بأصبهان قال انا أبو منصور شجاع بن علی بن شجاع المصقلى الصوفى قال انا أبو عبدالله محمد بن اسحق بن محمد بن يحيى العبدي، قال أنا أحمد بن سليمان بن ایوب بن حزام قال ثنا موسى بن أبي عوف قال ثنا سلمة بن خداش قال ثنا محمد بن القسم الطائي ان عبد الله في قريته فقال هاجر أبي وأمى إلى النبي صلى الله عليه كان ابن بسر معهم وسلم وان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مسح بيده رأسى وقال ليعيشن هذا الغلام ،قرنا قلت بأبي وأمي يارسول الله وكم القرن قال مائة سنة، قال عبد الله فلقد عشت خمسا وتسعين سنة وبقيت خمس سنين إلى أن أتم قول رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال محمد فحسبنا بعد ذلك خمس سنين ثم مات
And it also indicates what we were informed by Shaykh Abu al-Fath Yusuf ibn Abd al-Wahid ibn Muhammad ibn Yusuf al-Mahani in Isfahan, he said: Abu Mansur Shuja' ibn Ali ibn Shuja' al-Masqali al-Sufi narrated to us, he said: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ishaq ibn Muhammad ibn Yahya al-Abdi narrated to us, he said: Ahmad ibn Sulayman ibn Ayyub ibn Hizam narrated to us, he said: Musa ibn Abi Awf narrated to us, he said: Salama ibn Khadash narrated to us, he said: Muhammad ibn al-Qasim al-Ta'i narrated to us, that Abdullah (ibn Busr) was in his village and said: 'My father and mother emigrated to the Prophet ﷺ, and Ibn Busr was with them. And the Prophet ﷺ wiped his hand over my head and said: 'This boy will live a qarn.' I said: 'May my father and mother be ransomed for you, O Messenger of Allah! And how much is the qarn?' He said: 'One hundred years.' Abdullah said: 'I lived ninety-five years, and five years remain until I complete the saying of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ.' Muhammad said: 'Then we counted five years after that, then he died.'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage presents another hadith with a chain of transmission to confirm that a qarn equals one hundred years. The story involves Abdullah ibn Busr, whose head the Prophet wiped, saying he would live a qarn. When asked the length of a qarn, the Prophet explicitly said one hundred years. Abdullah lived ninety-five years and then five more years (totaling 100) to fulfill the prophecy. This serves as direct evidence that the qarn is exactly one hundred years.

Correction: The hadith records that he lived 95 years and then five more years, totaling 100, fulfilling the Prophet's statement.

?

?

The Definition of Qarn and Prophetic Chronology
Ibn Asakir reports the number of qurns between prophets from multiple narrations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that early scholars defined a qarn as one hundred years and used this to calculate the time between prophets.

Core Idea
A qarn is one hundred years: a fixed measure for prophetic history.

This lesson presents direct narrations from trusted scholars establishing that a qarn is consistently defined as one hundred years. The passages give specific counts between Adam, Noah, Abraham, and Moses, showing how early Muslims understood prophetic chronology. The multiple chains of transmission reinforce the reliability of this information.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrations carefully
Read both chains of transmission. Notice the names of narrators and how the information is passed down.
The chains show the careful preservation of knowledge.
2
Identify the consistent definition
In both narrations, a qarn is defined as one hundred years. Confirm that this definition is repeated.
3
Note the periods mentioned
The first narration mentions Adam to Noah and Noah to Abraham. The second adds Abraham to Moses. All periods are ten qurns.
This shows a pattern across prophetic history.
4
Reflect on multiple narrations
Ask yourself why two different chains are given. The repetition strengthens the reliability of the information.
It is a method of tawatur (mass transmission).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأخبرنا الشيخان أبو غالب أحمد وأبو عبدالله يحيى ابنا الحسن بن أحمد بن البناء ببغداد قالا انا أبو الحسين محمد بن أحمد بن محمد بن علی بن الابنوسى قال انا أبو بكر أحمد بن عبيد بن الفضل بن البيرى اجازة قال انا محمد بن الحسين بن محمد بن سعيد الزعفراني قال ثنا أبو بكر أحمد بن أبي خيثمة زهير بن حرب قال ثنا على بن بحر بن برى ويعقوب بن كعب الأنطاكي قالا حدثنا عيسى بن يونس، قال ثنا الأوزاعي عن يحيى بن أبي كثير عن أبي سلمة قال كان بين آدم ونوح عليهما السلام عشرة قرون القرن مائة عام وكان بين نوح وابراهيم عليهما السلام عشرة قرون، أخبرنا الشيخ أبو بكر محمد بن عبدالباقی بن محمد الفرضى قال أنا أبو محمد الحسن بن علی بن محمد الجوهرى قال انا أبو عمر محمد بن العباس بن محمد الخزاز، قال انا أبو الحسن احمد بن معروف بن بشر الخشاب قال انا أبو محمد حارث بن أبي أسامة قال أنا أبو عبد الله محمد ابن سعد قال أنا محمد بن عمر الواقدى عن غير واحد من أهل العلم قالوا كان بين آدم ونوح عشرة قرون القرن مائة عام، وبين نوح وابراهيم عشرة قرون والقرن ماية سنة وبين ابراهيم وموسى بن عمران عشرة قرون والقرن ماية سنة
And we were informed by the two shaykhs, Abu Ghalib Ahmad and Abu Abdullah Yahya, both sons of al-Hasan ibn Ahmad ibn al-Banna in Baghdad, they said: Abu al-Husayn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ali ibn al-Abnusi narrated to us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ubayd ibn al-Fadl ibn al-Bayri narrated to us by permission, he said: Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Muhammad ibn Sa'id al-Za'farani narrated to us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Abi Khaythama Zuhayr ibn Harb narrated to us, he said: Ali ibn Bahr ibn Barri and Ya'qub ibn Ka'b al-Antaki narrated to us, they said: Isa ibn Yunus narrated to us, he said: al-Awza'i narrated to us from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir from Abu Salama, he said: Between Adam and Noah, peace be upon them, were ten qurns, each qarn being one hundred years. And between Noah and Abraham, peace be upon them, were ten qurns. We were informed by Shaykh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Abd al-Baqi ibn Muhammad al-Faradi, he said: Abu Muhammad al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jawhari narrated to us, he said: Abu Umar Muhammad ibn al-Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Khazzaz narrated to us, he said: Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Ma'ruf ibn Bishr al-Khashshab narrated to us, he said: Abu Muhammad Harith ibn Abi Usama narrated to us, he said: Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Sa'd narrated to us, he said: Muhammad ibn Umar al-Waqidi narrated to us from more than one scholar, they said: Between Adam and Noah were ten qurns, each qarn one hundred years. Between Noah and Abraham were ten qurns, each qarn one hundred years. Between Abraham and Moses son of Imran were ten qurns, each qarn one hundred years.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage provides multiple narrations to confirm that a qarn is consistently defined as one hundred years throughout prophetic history. Two chains of narration are given: one from Abu Salama stating that there were ten qurns (each 100 years) between Adam and Noah, and between Noah and Abraham. Another narration from Waqidi and other scholars adds that there were also ten qurns between Abraham and Moses. This establishes the qarn as a fixed unit of one hundred years.

Key Terms
عشرة قرون
القرن مائة عام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The numbers of qurns between prophets are symbolic or inaccurate.
Correction: The text presents them as factual historical periods based on multiple reliable narrations.

Checkpoint
How many qurns were between Adam and Noah according to the narrations?
A) 10.
B) 100.
C) 5.
D) 20.

Key Takeaway
Early scholars consistently defined a qarn as one hundred years and used it to measure time between prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If each qarn is one hundred years, and there were ten qurns between Adam and Noah, that is a thousand years of history before the Flood. How does that vast span of time make you feel about the urgency of responding to Allah's guidance in your own life?
?
This report was transmitted through multiple careful chains of narrators. Does your trust in Islamic knowledge increase when you see such precision? What does that demand from you in how you seek and preserve religious knowledge?
?
Knowing that these time intervals were preserved accurately by early scholars, does it challenge any casual assumptions you had about the chronology of the prophets? How can this lesson motivate you to study Islamic history with more discipline?

Al-Ash'ari's Method: Reason and Revelation
Ibn Asakir praises al-Ash'ari's method of using rational and legal proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari established his theological positions using both rational proofs and legal evidences, and why this method is praised by Ibn Asakir.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's theology balances reason and revelation, not whim.

Ibn Asakir introduces us to the distinctive method of Imam al-Ash'ari. In this passage, he highlights that al-Ash'ari did not follow personal desire or innovation, but rather grounded his positions in rational proofs that have been tested and legal evidences that are measured. This approach makes his theology a balanced path to truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the contrast between what al-Ash'ari avoided and what he used.
The passage is dense with paired concepts.
2
Identify the two foundations
Find where Ibn Asakir mentions 'rational proofs' and 'legal evidences'. Note that both are used together.
The phrase 'براهين عقلية وأدلة شرعية' is key.
3
Reflect on the contrast
Consider why Ibn Asakir emphasizes that al-Ash'ari did not follow desire or innovation. What does this tell us about the integrity of his method?
This shows al-Ash'ari's approach is principled, not arbitrary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى غير ذلك من أصول يكثر تعدادها وتذكارها، وهذه الطرق التي سلكها لم يسلكها شهوة وإرادة، ولم يحدثها بدعة واستحسانا ولكنه أثبتها ببراهين عقلية مخبورة وأدلة شرعية مسبورة واعلام هادية إلى الحق وحجج داعية إلى الصواب والصدق، هى الطرق إلى الله سبحانه وتعالى والسبيل إلى النجاة والفوز من تمسك بها فاز ونجا ومن حاد عنها ضل وغوى .
فإذا كان أبو الحسن رضى الله عنه كما ذكر عنه من حسن مستوصب المذهب عند أهل المعرفة بالعلم والانتقاد يوافقه في أكثر ما يذهب إليه أكابر العباد ولا يقدح في معتقده غير أهل الجهل والعناد فلابد ان نحكى عنه معتقده على وجهه بالامانة ونجتنب ان نريد فيه أو ننقص منه تركا للخيانة ليعلم حقيقة حاله في صحة عقيدته في أصول الديانة فاسمع ماذكره في أول كتابه الذي سماه بالابانة فإنه قال الحمد لله الأحد الواحد العزيز الماجد المتفرد بالتوحيد المتمجد بالتمجيد، الذي لا تبلغه صفات العبيد وليس له مثل ولانديد وهو المبدى المعيد، جل عن الصاحية والأبناء وتقدس عن ملامسة النساء فليست له عرة تنال ولاحد تضرب له فيه الأمثال لم يزل بصفاته أولا قديرا ولا يزال عالما خبيرا، سبق الأشياء علمه ونفذت فيها إرادته فلم تعزب عنه خفيات الأمور، ولم تغيره اتخاذ
And beyond that are numerous principles whose enumeration and recollection would be lengthy. These paths which he followed, he did not follow them out of desire and whim, nor did he originate them as innovation and approval; rather, he established them by well-tested rational proofs and measured legal evidences, and guiding signs that lead to truth, and proofs that call to what is correct and truthful. They are the paths to Allah Almighty and the way to salvation and success. Whoever clings to them succeeds and is saved, and whoever deviates from them goes astray and is ruined.
Now, since Abu al-Hasan, may Allah be pleased with him, is as has been mentioned concerning him—with goodness and soundness of doctrine according to the people of knowledge and criticism, and the great worshipers agree with him in most of what he holds, and none impugn his creed except the people of ignorance and stubbornness—it is necessary for us to relate his creed accurately with honesty and refrain from adding or omitting anything, avoiding betrayal, so that his true state regarding the soundness of his belief in the fundamentals of religion may be known. So listen to what he mentioned at the beginning of his book which he named 'al-Ibana'. He said: 'Praise be to Allah, the One, the Unique, the Mighty, the Glorious, the Unique in oneness, the Exalted in exaltation, whom the attributes of servants do not reach, and there is nothing like Him nor equal to Him. He is the Originator and the Restorer. He is exalted above female companionship and sons, and sanctified above touching women. He has no spouse to be attained, nor is any similitude struck for Him. He has not ceased to be with His attributes—First, Powerful—and He does not cease to be Knowing, Aware. His knowledge preceded all things, and His will permeates them. The hidden matters of things are not concealed from Him, nor does taking (?) change Him...'
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage has two parts. First, Ibn 'Asakir summarizes the method of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari: the middle positions he took on various theological issues were not based on personal desire or innovation; they were grounded in rational proofs ('aqliyya) that have been tested (makhbura) and legal evidences (shar'iyya) that are measured (masbura). These constitute the path to salvation. Second, Ibn 'Asakir transitions to presenting al-Ash'ari's own creed as recorded in his book 'al-Ibana 'an Usul al-Diyana' (The Clarification of the Foundations of Religion). He urges honesty and accuracy in transmission. Then he quotes the opening of al-Ibana, which begins with praise of God, affirmation of His oneness, transcendence above human attributes, and His eternal attributes of knowledge and power. This sets the tone for al-Ash'ari's creedal exposition.

Key Terms
براهين عقلية
أدلة شرعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari relied only on reason and ignored revelation.
Correction: Ibn Asakir states that al-Ash'ari used both rational proofs and legal evidences (which include revelation). His method integrates reason and scripture.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, what did al-Ash'ari use to establish his theological positions?
A) Personal desire and whim.
B) Only rational arguments without revelation.
C) Well-tested rational proofs and measured legal evidences.
D) Blind imitation of earlier scholars.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's method combines rational proofs and legal evidences, making his creed both intellectually sound and rooted in revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek religious knowledge, do you test your beliefs using both reason and revelation, or do you rely on feelings and customs? How might al-Ash'ari's example challenge you to examine your own sources of conviction?
?
Are there areas of your faith where you follow your own desire (shahwa) instead of disciplined, evidence-based understanding? What would it cost you to abandon that whim and cling to the tested proofs?
?
If clinging to these paths leads to salvation, what deviation (even small) might you tolerate in your own beliefs that could lead you astray? Will you identify one such area today and commit to correcting it using both rational and revealed proofs?

The Opening of al-Ibana: Affirming Tawhid and Divine Attributes
Ibn Asakir introduces al-Ash'ari's creed from his book al-Ibana, quoting its opening.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the key elements of al-Ash'ari's creed as stated at the beginning of his book al-Ibana, including affirmation of God's oneness, transcendence, and eternal attributes.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari begins his creed by exalting Allah above all creation and affirming His eternal attributes.

Imam al-Ash'ari opens his book al-Ibana with a powerful declaration of tawhid. This passage, as recorded by Ibn Asakir, affirms Allah's oneness, His transcendence beyond human attributes, and His eternal attributes of power and knowledge. It sets the foundation for the entire creedal exposition that follows.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic praise and its translation. Notice the rhythm and the focus on divine transcendence.
The style is reminiscent of Quranic language.
2
Identify the affirmations
List the key doctrines: God's oneness, His transcendence (no spouse, children, etc.), and His eternal attributes (Power, Knowledge).
Each phrase builds on the previous.
3
Connect to method
Remember from the first lesson that al-Ash'ari uses reason and revelation. How does this opening reflect that?
It is scriptural in tone but also rationally coherent.

A) Allah has a spouse and children.

D) Allah's will does not permeate all things.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's creed begins by affirming God's absolute oneness, transcendence, and eternal attributes, establishing a middle path between negation and anthropomorphism.

?

?
When you say 'Allahu Akbar', does your heart feel the absolute majesty of the One whom 'the attributes of servants do not reach'? How can you make your next prayer reflect that profound distance?
?
Al-Ash'ari begins his creed with praise (al-hamd). When was the last time you praised Allah with mindful reflection on His oneness and eternity? Commit to a specific time this day to worship Him with that awareness.

The Duty to Uphold the Sunna and Avoid Blind Taqlid
The author praises the Sunna and warns against abandoning it for taqlid of forefathers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that holding fast to the Sunna is a divine command and that abandoning it for blind imitation of ancestors is a grave error.

Core Idea
The Sunna is Allah's strong rope; hold it or be lost.

This passage opens by declaring the Sunna as the straight path and strongest tie to Allah, then immediately grounds this claim in multiple Quranic verses that command obedience to the Prophet. The author contrasts this divine imperative with the behavior of those who, overcome by worldly affliction, discard the Sunna and blindly follow their forefathers. Reading this section will clarify why adherence to the Sunna is not optional but a core obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central analogy
Notice how the author describes the Sunna as 'Allah's straight path and strong rope.' What does this imagery imply about the function of the Sunna?
2
Trace the Quranic evidence
Read each quoted verse carefully. What specific command does each verse give regarding the Prophet and his Sunna? How does the author use these verses to build the case?
The verses are from 59:7, 24:63, 4:83, 42:10, 53:3-4, 10:15, 24:51, and 4:59.
3
Understand the condemnation
After the verses, the author denounces those who 'cast the Sunna behind their backs and inclined to their forefathers.' Why is this a dangerous deviation? What does 'blind taqlid' mean here?
The passage explicitly links this to being misguided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلقاء علم الأولين والآخرين وأكمل به الفرائض والدين وهو صراط الله المستقيم وحبله المتين من تمسك به نجا ومن خالفه ضل وغوى وحثنا في كتابه على التمسك بسنة رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال (ما أتاكم الرسول فخذوه ومانهاكم عنه فانتهوا ) وقال ( فليحذر الذين يخالفون عن أمره وقال ( ولو ردوه إلى الرسول وإلى أولى الأمر منهم لعلمه الذين يستنبطونه منهم) وقال (وما اختلفتم فيه من شيء فحكمه إلى الله) يقول إلى كتاب الله وسنة نبيه صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال (وما ينطق عن الهوى إن هو إلا وحي يوحى) وقال (قل ما يكون لى ان ابدله من نفسي ان اتبع إلا ما يوحى إلى) وقال ( إنما كان قول المؤمنين إذا دعوا إلى الله ورسوله ليحكم بينهم ان يقولوا سمعنا واطعنا ) وأمرهم أن يسمعوا قوله ويطيعوا أمره وقال ) أطيعوا الله وأطيعوا الرسول ) فأمرهم بطاعة رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم كما أمرهم بطاعته ودعاهم إلى التمسك بسنة نبيه صلى الله عليه وسلم كما أمرهم بالعمل بكتابه فنبذ كثير ممن غلبت عليه شقوته واستحوذت عليه بليته سنة نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وراء ظهورهم، ومالوا إلى أسلافهم وقلدوهم دينهم ودانوا بديانتهم وابطلوا سنن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورفضوها وانكروها وجحدوها، افتراء منهم الله قد ضلوا وماكانوا مهتدين. واوصيكم عباد الله بتقوى الله واحذركم الدنيا فإنها حلوة خضرة تغر أهلها وتخدع سكانها، قال الله عز وجل (واضرب لهم مثل الحياة الدنيا كماء أنزلناه من السماء فاختلط به نبات الأرض فاصبح هشيما تذروه الرياح وكان الله على كل شيء مقتدرا ان امرا لم يكن منها في حيرة إلا أعقبته بعدها عبرة لم يلق من سرائها بطنا إلا منحته من ضرائها ظهورا ا غرارة غرور ما فيها فانية فإن من عليها كما حكم عليها ربها بقوله (كل) من عليها فان فاعملوا رحمكم الله للحياة الدائمة والخلود الأبد فإن الدنيا تنقضى عن أهلها وتبقى الأعمال قلائد فى رقاب أهلها . واعلموا أنكم ميتون ثم إنكم من بعد موتكم إلى ربكم تصيرون، ليجزي الذين أساءوا بما عملوا ويجزى الذين أحسنوا بالحسنى وكونوا بطاعة ربكم عاملين وعما نهاكم عنه منتهين
From the knowledge of the first and the last, He completed with it the obligations and the religion, and it is the straight path of Allah and His strong rope. Whoever holds fast to it is saved, and whoever opposes it goes astray and errs. He urged us in His Book to hold fast to the Sunna of His Messenger (ﷺ), saying: 'Whatever the Messenger gives you, take it; and whatever he forbids you, abstain from it' (59:7), and He said: 'Let those who oppose his command beware' (24:63), and He said: 'If they had referred it to the Messenger and to those in authority among them, those who can derive it from them would have known it' (4:83), and He said: 'Whatever you differ about, its judgment is with Allah' (42:10) – meaning to the Book of Allah and the Sunna of His Prophet (ﷺ) – and He said: 'He does not speak from desire; it is only a revelation revealed' (53:3-4), and He said: 'Say: I cannot alter it of my own accord; I only follow what is revealed to me' (10:15), and He said: 'The only saying of the believers when they are called to Allah and His Messenger to judge between them is that they say, "We hear and we obey"' (24:51). And He commanded them to hear His word and obey His command, and He said: 'Obey Allah and obey the Messenger' (4:59). So He commanded them to obey His Messenger (ﷺ) just as He commanded them to obey Him, and called them to hold fast to the Sunna of His Prophet (ﷺ) just as He commanded them to act by His Book. But many of those whose wretchedness overcame them and whose affliction took hold of them cast the Sunna of the Prophet of Allah (ﷺ) behind their backs, and inclined to their forefathers and blindly imitated them in their religion, adopted their faith, and nullified the Sunan of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), rejected them, denied them, and disbelieved in them – slandering Allah; they have surely gone astray and are not guided. I exhort you, O servants of Allah, to fear Allah, and I warn you against the world, for it is sweet and green, deceiving its people and deluding its inhabitants. Allah the Exalted said: 'And present to them the example of the life of this world: like water which We send down from the sky, and the vegetation of the earth mingles with it, and then it becomes dry stubble that the winds scatter. And Allah is over all things competent' (18:45). If a person is not in confusion about it, it will be followed by a lesson. No one takes from its joys a belly except that it gives him from its harms backs. O deceptive deception! What is in it is perishing, for everything on it is passing, as its Lord has decreed by His saying: 'Everyone upon it is perishing' (55:26). So work, may Allah have mercy on you, for the everlasting life and eternal eternity, for the world passes away from its people and deeds remain as necklaces around their necks. And know that you will die, then after your death you will return to your Lord, to recompense those who did evil with what they did and to reward those who did good with the best. And be obedient to your Lord and refrain from what He has forbidden you.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage serves as a powerful exhortation. It begins by praising the Sunna as the straight path and strong rope of Allah, citing numerous Quranic verses that command obedience to the Prophet (ﷺ) and adherence to his Sunna. The author then laments that many people, overcome by misfortune, have abandoned the Sunna, blindly following their forefathers and rejecting the established practices of the Messenger. He warns against the deceptive nature of this world, quoting Quran 18:45 and reminding that worldly joys are fleeting and are followed by hardships. He concludes with a reminder of death and the return to Allah, urging his audience to obey Allah and stay away from His prohibitions. The overall tone is one of warning and encouragement to cling to the revealed guidance of the Quran and Sunna, and to avoid blind imitation (taqlid) of ancestors.

Key Terms
السنة
التمسك
الطاعة
التقليد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Blindly following the traditions of one's forefathers is acceptable and equivalent to following the Sunna.
Correction: The passage explicitly condemns those who 'cast the Sunna behind their backs and inclined to their forefathers,' stating they have 'gone astray.' Taqlid of ancestors is not a valid substitute for the revealed guidance.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what did those overcome by wretchedness do with the Sunna?
A) They defended it vigorously.
B) They cast it behind their backs and followed their forefathers.
C) They compiled it into books.
D) They preached it to others.

Key Takeaway
The Sunna is a divine command; abandoning it for blind taqlid of ancestors is a path to misguidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life have you silently preferred the ways of your family or culture over a clear command from the Quran or Sunna? Will you stop today?
?
When you read the verse 'Let those who oppose his command beware', what specific command of the Prophet do you find hardest to obey? What will you do about it this week?
?
The author says those who reject the Sunna 'slander Allah'. Do you ever downplay the importance of a hadith because it is inconvenient? How will you change your attitude starting today?

Warning Against the Deception of the World
The author warns against the deceptive nature of the world and calls to prepare for the afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fleeting nature of worldly life, its deceptive appeal, and the necessity of preparing for the afterlife through obedience to Allah.

Core Idea
The world is sweet but fleeting; only deeds remain.

After addressing the issue of abandoning the Sunna, the author turns to a broader spiritual warning about the nature of this worldly life. Citing a vivid Quranic parable, he reminds his audience that the world is deceptive, its pleasures temporary, and that everyone will die and return to Allah for judgment. This section calls for active obedience and caution against being deluded by worldly attractions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic parable
Read the verse from Surah Al-Kahf (18:45) that compares worldly life to vegetation that withers. What does this imagery teach about the world?
The verse is: 'And present to them the example of the life of this world: like water which We send down from the sky... then it becomes dry stubble that the winds scatter.'
2
Note the warnings
The author says the world is 'sweet and green' and deceives its people. What are the consequences mentioned? How does the author describe the cycle of joy and hardship?
The phrase 'If a person is not in confusion about it, it will be followed by a lesson' indicates that worldly pleasures are inevitably followed by trials.
3
Understand the final exhortation
The passage ends with a call to work for the everlasting life, reminding that deeds remain as 'necklaces around necks.' What action does the author urge?
He urges obedience to Allah and refraining from His prohibitions.
