تلقاء علم الأولين والآخرين وأكمل به الفرائض والدين وهو صراط الله المستقيم وحبله المتين من تمسك به نجا ومن خالفه ضل وغوى وحثنا في كتابه على التمسك بسنة رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال (ما أتاكم الرسول فخذوه ومانهاكم عنه فانتهوا ) وقال ( فليحذر الذين يخالفون عن أمره وقال ( ولو ردوه إلى الرسول وإلى أولى الأمر منهم لعلمه الذين يستنبطونه منهم) وقال (وما اختلفتم فيه من شيء فحكمه إلى الله) يقول إلى كتاب الله وسنة نبيه صلى الله عليه وسلم وقال (وما ينطق عن الهوى إن هو إلا وحي يوحى) وقال (قل ما يكون لى ان ابدله من نفسي ان اتبع إلا ما يوحى إلى) وقال ( إنما كان قول المؤمنين إذا دعوا إلى الله ورسوله ليحكم بينهم ان يقولوا سمعنا واطعنا ) وأمرهم أن يسمعوا قوله ويطيعوا أمره وقال ) أطيعوا الله وأطيعوا الرسول ) فأمرهم بطاعة رسوله صلى الله عليه وسلم كما أمرهم بطاعته ودعاهم إلى التمسك بسنة نبيه صلى الله عليه وسلم كما أمرهم بالعمل بكتابه فنبذ كثير ممن غلبت عليه شقوته واستحوذت عليه بليته سنة نبي الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وراء ظهورهم، ومالوا إلى أسلافهم وقلدوهم دينهم ودانوا بديانتهم وابطلوا سنن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ورفضوها وانكروها وجحدوها، افتراء منهم الله قد ضلوا وماكانوا مهتدين. واوصيكم عباد الله بتقوى الله واحذركم الدنيا فإنها حلوة خضرة تغر أهلها وتخدع سكانها، قال الله عز وجل (واضرب لهم مثل الحياة الدنيا كماء أنزلناه من السماء فاختلط به نبات الأرض فاصبح هشيما تذروه الرياح وكان الله على كل شيء مقتدرا ان امرا لم يكن منها في حيرة إلا أعقبته بعدها عبرة لم يلق من سرائها بطنا إلا منحته من ضرائها ظهورا ا غرارة غرور ما فيها فانية فإن من عليها كما حكم عليها ربها بقوله (كل) من عليها فان فاعملوا رحمكم الله للحياة الدائمة والخلود الأبد فإن الدنيا تنقضى عن أهلها وتبقى الأعمال قلائد فى رقاب أهلها . واعلموا أنكم ميتون ثم إنكم من بعد موتكم إلى ربكم تصيرون، ليجزي الذين أساءوا بما عملوا ويجزى الذين أحسنوا بالحسنى وكونوا بطاعة ربكم عاملين وعما نهاكم عنه منتهين
From the knowledge of the first and the last, He completed with it the obligations and the religion, and it is the straight path of Allah and His strong rope. Whoever holds fast to it is saved, and whoever opposes it goes astray and errs. He urged us in His Book to hold fast to the Sunna of His Messenger (ﷺ), saying: 'Whatever the Messenger gives you, take it; and whatever he forbids you, abstain from it' (59:7), and He said: 'Let those who oppose his command beware' (24:63), and He said: 'If they had referred it to the Messenger and to those in authority among them, those who can derive it from them would have known it' (4:83), and He said: 'Whatever you differ about, its judgment is with Allah' (42:10) – meaning to the Book of Allah and the Sunna of His Prophet (ﷺ) – and He said: 'He does not speak from desire; it is only a revelation revealed' (53:3-4), and He said: 'Say: I cannot alter it of my own accord; I only follow what is revealed to me' (10:15), and He said: 'The only saying of the believers when they are called to Allah and His Messenger to judge between them is that they say, "We hear and we obey"' (24:51). And He commanded them to hear His word and obey His command, and He said: 'Obey Allah and obey the Messenger' (4:59). So He commanded them to obey His Messenger (ﷺ) just as He commanded them to obey Him, and called them to hold fast to the Sunna of His Prophet (ﷺ) just as He commanded them to act by His Book. But many of those whose wretchedness overcame them and whose affliction took hold of them cast the Sunna of the Prophet of Allah (ﷺ) behind their backs, and inclined to their forefathers and blindly imitated them in their religion, adopted their faith, and nullified the Sunan of the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), rejected them, denied them, and disbelieved in them – slandering Allah; they have surely gone astray and are not guided. I exhort you, O servants of Allah, to fear Allah, and I warn you against the world, for it is sweet and green, deceiving its people and deluding its inhabitants. Allah the Exalted said: 'And present to them the example of the life of this world: like water which We send down from the sky, and the vegetation of the earth mingles with it, and then it becomes dry stubble that the winds scatter. And Allah is over all things competent' (18:45). If a person is not in confusion about it, it will be followed by a lesson. No one takes from its joys a belly except that it gives him from its harms backs. O deceptive deception! What is in it is perishing, for everything on it is passing, as its Lord has decreed by His saying: 'Everyone upon it is perishing' (55:26). So work, may Allah have mercy on you, for the everlasting life and eternal eternity, for the world passes away from its people and deeds remain as necklaces around their necks. And know that you will die, then after your death you will return to your Lord, to recompense those who did evil with what they did and to reward those who did good with the best. And be obedient to your Lord and refrain from what He has forbidden you.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage serves as a powerful exhortation. It begins by praising the Sunna as the straight path and strong rope of Allah, citing numerous Quranic verses that command obedience to the Prophet (ﷺ) and adherence to his Sunna. The author then laments that many people, overcome by misfortune, have abandoned the Sunna, blindly following their forefathers and rejecting the established practices of the Messenger. He warns against the deceptive nature of this world, quoting Quran 18:45 and reminding that worldly joys are fleeting and are followed by hardships. He concludes with a reminder of death and the return to Allah, urging his audience to obey Allah and stay away from His prohibitions. The overall tone is one of warning and encouragement to cling to the revealed guidance of the Quran and Sunna, and to avoid blind imitation (taqlid) of ancestors.

Misconception: The world is a permanent place of enjoyment, and one can indulge in it without consequence.
Correction: The passage clearly states that the world is 'deceptive,' 'perishing,' and that everyone will die and be judged. It warns that joys are followed by harms and that only deeds remain.

C) A solid mountain.

Key Takeaway
The world is deceptive and temporary; true success lies in preparing for the eternal afterlife through obedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says deeds remain as necklaces around your neck. What deed are you currently doing that you would be ashamed to have around your neck on the Day of Judgment? And what will you change today?
?
You have just read that worldly joys always bring subsequent harms. Think of a pleasure you are chasing right now. Are you willing to accept the harm that will follow, or will you let it go for the sake of what lasts?

Introduction to the Creed of Ahl al-Sunnah: The Opening Doxology
Ibn Asakir opens the chapter with a doxology and a list of divine attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational doxology of Ibn Asakir's creedal exposition, which establishes the attributes of Allah as affirmed by Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Allah is described by attributes of perfection that are eternal, unique, and beyond creation.

Ibn Asakir begins his chapter by praising Allah with a series of attributes that form the bedrock of Ahl al-Sunnah's creed. This opening doxology prepares the reader for the detailed exposition of the two testimonies, anchoring the creed in the recognition of Allah's unmatched majesty and eternal nature.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening basmala and title
Notice the formal beginning: 'In the name of Allah...' and the title of the book and chapter. This sets the context for the creedal discussion.
The book is 'Foundations of the Creeds' and the chapter focuses on the two testimonies.
2
Identify the praises of Allah
Ibn Asakir praises Allah with attributes like 'the Originator, the Restorer', 'Possessor of the Glorious Throne', and 'Guide of the chosen servants'. Reflect on how these establish Allah's power and lordship.
3
Focus on the list of attributes
The passage then lists attributes such as 'One with no partner', 'Unique with no peer', 'Eternal with no beginning', 'Everlasting with no end'. This is the core creedal statement.
These attributes directly counter false beliefs in partnerships or temporal limitations.
4
Understand the conclusion
The passage ends with 'He is the First and the Last, the Inward and the Outward'. This summarizes Allah's transcendence and immanence.
This verse-like phrasing is a key tenet of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم كتاب قواعد العقايد وفيه أربعة فصول، الفصل الأول في ترجمة عقيدة أهل السنة في كلمتي الشهادة التي هي أحد مباني الإسلام ، فنقول وبالله التوفيق الحمد لله المبدئ المعيد الفعال لما يريد ذي العرش المجيد ، والبطش الشديد ، الهادي صفوة العبيد إلى المنهج الرشيد والمسلك السديد ، المنعم عليهم بعد شهادة التوحيد بحراسة عقائدهم عن ظلمات التشكيك والترديد السابق بهم إلى اتباع رسوله المصطفى واقتفاء صحبه الكرمين بالتأييد والتسديد ، المتجلي لهم في ذاته وأفعاله بمحاسن أوصافه التي لا يدركها إلا من ألقى السمع وهو شهيد ، المعرف إياهم في ذاته أنه واحد لا شريك له فرد لا مثل له صمد لا ضد له ، منفرد لا ند له وأنه قديم لا أول له أزلي لا بداية له ، مستمر الوجود لا آخر له أبدي لا نهاية له قيوم لا انقطاع له ، دائم لا انصرام له لم يزل ولا يزال موصوفاً بنعوت الجلال لا يقضى عليه بالانقضاء تصرم الآباد وانقراض الآجال بل هو الأول والآخر والباطن والظاهر .
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The book of the Foundations of the Creeds, and it contains four chapters. The first chapter is on the exposition of the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding the two testimonies, which are among the pillars of Islam. We say, and with Allah is success: Praise be to Allah, the Originator, the Restorer, the Doer of what He wills, Possessor of the Glorious Throne, and of severe might, the Guide of the chosen servants to the right path and the correct way, the Bestower of favors upon them after the testimony of monotheism by guarding their creeds from the darknesses of doubt and hesitation, who preceded them to follow His Chosen Messenger and to emulate His noble Companions with support and success, who manifests Himself to them in His essence and His actions through the beauties of His attributes which none comprehend except one who listens attentively while being witness, who makes known to them in His essence that He is One with no partner, Unique with no peer, Self-Sufficient with no opposite, Sole with no equal, and that He is Eternal with no beginning, Everlasting with no end, continuously Existent with no cessation, Self-Sustaining with no interruption, Permanent with no termination, He has always been and always will be described with the attributes of majesty, He is not decreed to have termination by the passing of ages and the expiration of terms, rather He is the First and the Last, the Inward and the Outward.
Source pages p. 229

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter. It begins with the basmala and the title of the book, then states that the chapter contains four sections, the first of which is on the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah regarding the two testimonies (the shahada). Then it praises Allah with a series of attributes: He is the Originator and Restorer, the Doer of what He wills, Possessor of the Glorious Throne and severe might, the Guide of the chosen servants. It then describes how He guards the creeds of the believers from doubts and directs them to follow His Messenger and Companions. The passage then lists foundational attributes of Allah: He is one without partner, unique without peer, self-sufficient without opposite, sole without equal. He is eternal without beginning, everlasting without end, continuously existent, self-sustaining, permanent. He has always been and always will be described with attributes of majesty. He is not subject to termination by the passing of ages or expiration of terms. He is the First, the Last, the Apparent, and the Hidden. This sets the stage for the detailed creedal exposition that follows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that affirming attributes for Allah implies multiplicity or similarity to creation.
Correction: Ibn Asakir’s opening negates any partner, peer, opposite, or equal, and emphasizes that Allah’s attributes are unique and beyond creation.

Checkpoint
What does Ibn Asakir state about Allah's attributes in the introduction?
A) He is like His creation
B) He is eternal without beginning and lasting without end
C) He has a physical body
D) He is limited by time

Key Takeaway
The opening doxology establishes that Allah is eternal, unique, and possesses attributes of majesty that distinguish Him from all creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage says Allah guides 'chosen servants to the right path' and guards their creeds from doubts. Are you one of those chosen servants? If so, how is your creed being guarded right now? If not, what is stopping you from being among them?
?
The text says Allah 'manifests Himself … through the beauties of His attributes' but 'none comprehend except one who listens attentively while being witness.' Are you truly listening attentively when you reflect on Allah's names and attributes? Or do you let distractions cloud your heart?
?
Allah is described as 'the First and the Last, the Inward and the Outward.' In what area of your life have you forgotten that He is with you in your innermost thoughts (the Inward) and that He will be the Last after everything you love has passed? How does that change what you prioritize today?

Concluding Remarks on the Purpose of the Work
Ibn Asakir explains his methodology and urges contentment with his selection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Asakir's reasoning for limiting his biographical entries and the spiritual value of mentioning the righteous.

Core Idea
Ibn Asakir chose brevity over completeness to honor al-Ash'ari through his followers.

In wrapping up his biographical section, Ibn Asakir addresses the inevitable gaps in his work. He explains that his selection was intentional, aiming to avoid tediousness while still reflecting the virtue of Imam al-Ash'ari through his companions. This passage reveals his scholarly humility and his exhortation to readers to appreciate what is recorded.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own voice come through.
This passage is a personal reflection, so notice the tone.
2
Identify the main reason for brevity
Find where Ibn Asakir states why he did not include all companions. He explicitly mentions fear of boredom and preference for brevity.
He also says those omitted are more than those included.
3
Analyze the star analogy
Notice his comparison: counting scholars is like counting stars. This emphasizes the impossibility of completeness.
This shows his humility and honesty about the limits of his work.
4
Consider the purpose of the work
He states the purpose is to show al-Ash'ari's virtue through his companions. Reflect on how even a selective list achieves that.
The aim is not exhaustive biography but focused honor.
5
Reflect on the concluding saying
The phrase 'When the righteous are mentioned, mercy descends' is a traditional saying. What impact does it have on the reader?
It reminds us of the spiritual benefit of such accounts.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا آخر ما يسر الله عز وجل لى ذكره ممن اشتهر من العلماء من أصحابه وشرحت أمره، ومن لم أذكر منهم أكثر ممن ذكرت والمقصود إظهار فضله بفضل أصحابه كما أشرت، ولولا خوفي من الاملال للاسهاب إيثارى الاختصار لهذا الكتاب لتتبعت ذكر جميع الاصحاب وأطنبت في مدحهم غاية الإطناب وكنت أكون بعد بذل الجهد فيه مقصرا ومن تقصیری بالخلال بذكر كثير منهم معتذرا فكما لا يمكنني إحصاء نجوم السماء كذلك لا أتمكن من استقصاء ذكر جميع العلماء مع تقادم الأزمان والأعصار وكثرة المشتهرين فى البلدان والأمصار وانتشارهم في الأقطار والآفاق من المغرب والشام وخراسان والعراق فاقنعوا من ذكر حزبه بمن سمى ووصف واعرفوا فضل من لم يسم لكم بمن سمى وعرف ولا تسأموا أن مدح الأعيان وقرض الأئمة فعند ذكر الصالحين تنزل الرحمة.
This is the last of what Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, facilitated for me to mention of those who became well-known among the scholars of his (al-Ash'ari's) companions, and I have explained their affair. Those whom I did not mention are more than those I mentioned. The purpose is to show his virtue through the virtue of his companions, as I indicated. Were it not for my fear of causing boredom by prolixity, and my preference for brevity in this book, I would have pursued the mention of all the companions and would have exceeded in praising them to the utmost of praise. Even then, after exerting effort, I would fall short and apologize for my deficiency by mentioning many of them. Just as I cannot count the stars of heaven, so too I cannot cover the mention of all the scholars due to the passage of times and ages, the abundance of those famous in lands and regions, and their spread in the countries and horizons from Morocco, Syria, Khurasan, and Iraq. So be content with the mention of his party (hizb) by those I named and described, and recognize the virtue of those not named for you by those named and known. And do not be weary that praising notables and venerating imams (occurs) because when the righteous are mentioned, mercy descends.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage serves as the conclusion of the biographical section, where Ibn Asakir reflects on his method. He admits that many more scholars could have been included but he chose brevity to avoid tedium. The central purpose remains: to honor Imam al-Ash'ari by highlighting virtue of his followers. He compares counting scholars to counting stars, emphasizing impossibility of completeness. He urges readers to be satisfied with those listed and to infer the virtue of the unnamed from the named. The final phrase, 'When the righteous are mentioned, mercy descends,' is a well-known saying, reinforcing the spiritual benefit of these accounts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ibn Asakir's omission of some scholars implies they are less important.
Correction: Ibn Asakir explicitly states that those omitted are more numerous than those included, and that he could not possibly include all due to time and space constraints.

Checkpoint

A) He did not have enough information about them
B) He feared causing boredom and preferred brevity
C) They were not as virtuous as those listed
D) The book was too short

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir's selective approach was deliberate: he prioritized brevity and focused on honoring al-Ash'ari through a representative sample, urging readers to find contentment and recognize virtue even in the omissions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Ibn Asakir admits that those he could not mention far outnumber those he did. Think about your own life: are you more often weighed down by what you have not achieved, or grateful for what Allah has enabled you to do? How can the ‘contentment’ Ibn Asakir commands shift your perspective on your own limitations?
?
Ibn Asakir’s purpose was to honor al-Ash’ari by highlighting his companions. Who are the people in your life whose character reflects the teachings you claim to follow? If your own virtues were judged by the company you keep, what would be revealed? Are you actively seeking righteous company to polish your own soul?
?
The passage ends with a profound statement: when the righteous are mentioned, mercy descends. When was the last time you sincerely remembered a righteous person—not idly, but with a heart seeking that mercy? What prevents you from making such remembrance a regular practice, and how might it soften your heart if you did?

Author's Apology for Limited Coverage
Author apologizes for not mentioning all companions and explains his purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam Ibn Asakir limits his mention of al-Ash'ari's companions and the purpose behind his work.

Core Idea
The author apologizes for incompleteness but his aim is to show virtue, not to count every companion.

This passage is an important window into the author’s methodology and humility. Ibn Asakir explains that his book is not meant to be exhaustive, and he offers several reasons for focusing only on some companions. His apology reveals his scholarly integrity and his desire to focus on quality over quantity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the tone of apology and humility.
Pay attention to the metaphor of counting stars.
2
Identify the author's reasons
Find the two reasons the author gives for not mentioning all companions: fear of causing boredom (al-imalal) and the impossibility of enumerating them all (like counting stars).
The author also mentions his preference for conciseness.
3
Understand the positive purpose
Recognize that the author's goal is not completeness but showing the virtue of al-Ash'ari through his companions, and that mentioning the righteous brings mercy.
This reflects a common theme in Islamic biographical works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فهذا آخر ما يسر الله عز وجل لي ذكره ممن اشتهر من العلماء من أصحابه وشرحت أمره، ومن لم أذكر منهم أكثر ممن ذكرت والمقصود إظهار فضله بفضل أصحابه كما أشرت، ولولا خوفي من الإملال للإسهاب إيثاري الاختصار لهذا الكتاب لتتبعت ذكر جميع الأصحاب وأطنبت في مدحهم غاية الإطناب وكنت أكون بعد بذل الجهد فيه مقصرا ومن تقصيري بالخلال بذكر كثير منهم معتذرا فكما لا يمكنني إحصاء نجوم السماء كذلك لا أتمكن من استقصاء ذكر جميع العلماء مع تقادم الأزمان والأعصار وكثرة المشتهرين في البلدان والأمصار وانتشارهم في الأقطار والآفاق من المغرب والشام وخراسان والعراق فاقنعوا من ذكر حزبه بمن سمى ووصف واعرفوا فضل من لم يسم لكم بمن سمى وعرف ولا تسأموا أن مدح الأعيان وقرض الأئمة فعند ذكر الصالحين تنزل الرحمة
This is the last of what God Almighty facilitated for me to mention of those who became famous among the scholars from his companions, and I explained their affair. And those I did not mention among them are more than those I mentioned. The purpose is to show his virtue through the virtue of his companions as I alluded. And were it not for my fear of causing boredom due to prolixity, preferring conciseness for this book, I would have pursued mentioning all the companions and exaggerated in praising them to the utmost, and I would still, after exerting effort in it, be falling short, and I apologize for my shortcomings in the gaps by mentioning many of them. For just as I cannot count the stars of the sky, likewise I am unable to encompass the mention of all scholars due to the passage of time and ages, and the abundance of those famous in the cities and regions, and their spread in the quarters and horizons from the Maghrib, Syria, Khurasan, and Iraq. So be content with the mention of his party by those whom I named and described, and recognize the virtue of those not named to you by those who were named and known. And do not be weary that praising the notables and lauding the imams—for at the mention of the righteous mercy descends.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an authorial aside where Ibn Asakir explains the scope and purpose of his work. He states that he only mentioned some of al-Ash'ari's companions, not all, and his aim is to highlight al-Ash'ari's virtue through his companions. He apologizes for not being able to mention everyone, likening the task to counting stars. He also invokes a well-known concept that mentioning the righteous brings down mercy.

Why did the author not mention all of al-Ash'ari's companions?
A) He forgot many
B) He feared causing boredom by prolixity
C) He only knew a few
D) He wanted to keep the book short

Key Takeaway
The author humbly acknowledges his limitation while asserting that the purpose is not comprehensiveness but showing virtue and invoking mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you felt your own efforts in seeking knowledge were incomplete or insufficient? How does the author's humility in acknowledging his limitations while still striving to do good inspire you to continue despite your own shortcomings? What step will you take this week to persist in learning even when you feel overwhelmed by the vastness of what you don't know?
?
The author asks us to recognize the virtue of those not named by those who are named. Are there people in your community or in Islamic history whose worth you have underestimated because of limited exposure? How can you cultivate a habit of assuming virtue in those you haven't encountered, based on the virtue you see in others?
?
The author chose conciseness out of fear of causing boredom. Have you ever held back from sharing beneficial knowledge because you worried how others would receive it? What would change in your conversations if you prioritized the sake of Allah over the fear of others' reactions? Commit to sharing one beneficial thing you learned from this lesson with someone this week.

Al-Bayhaqi's Defense: Two Interpretations of the Condemnation of Kalam
Al-Bayhaqi explains two interpretations of the condemnation of kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Bayhaqi's two interpretations of the early condemnation of kalam and how they defend the legitimate use of kalam within Ahl al-Sunnah.

Core Idea
Not all kalam is blameworthy; only the kalam of innovators or kalam that displaces fiqh and action.

Early scholars like Abu Yusuf and Malik reportedly condemned kalam, but al-Bayhaqi clarifies that this condemnation was directed at the kalam of innovators, not the kalam of Ahl al-Sunnah. He also offers a second interpretation: the blame falls on those who focus solely on kalam while neglecting fiqh and practice. This passage shows how later scholars harmonized these reports with their own engagement in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the full translation. Notice the chain of transmission and al-Bayhaqi's two interpretations.
The isnad shows the reliability of the narration, but focus on the content of the defense.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Al-Bayhaqi first says the condemned kalam is the speech of innovators; second, it means neglecting fiqh and action. Write each interpretation in your own words.
The first interpretation is historical: in their era, only innovators engaged in kalam.
3
Examine the supporting sayings
Read the quotes from Hatim al-Asamm and Abu Bakr al-Warraq. They show that kalam, fiqh, and action are interdependent. Note how they classify neglect of each.
These quotes reinforce that balance is key.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرناها الشيخ أبو المعالي محمد بن إسماعيل بن محمد بن الحسين الفارسي قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد ابن الحسين بن على البيهقي ، قال أنا أبو سعد أحمد بن محمد الماليني ح ، وأخبرناها الشيخ أبو القسم إسماعيل ابن أحمد بن السمرقندي ، قال أخبرنا أبو القسم إسماعيل بن مسعدة الجرجاني ، قال لنا أبو القسم حمزة بن يوسف السهمي ، قالا أخبرنا أبو أحمد بن عدى ، قال ثنا جعفر ابن محمد بن الحسن بن المستفاض الفريابي ، قال حدثنى بشر بن الوليد ، قال سمعت أبا يوسف يقول من طلب الدين بالكلام تزندق ، وقال السهمى ومن طلب غريب الحديث كذب ومن طلب المال بالكيمياء الس ، قال أبو بكر البيهقى وروى هذا مالك بن أنس قال وإنما يريد والله أعلم بالكلام كلام أهل البدع ، فإن في عصرهما إنما كان يعرف بالكلام أهل البدع ، فأما أهل السنة فقلما كانوا يخوضون في الكلام حتى اضطروا إليه بعد ، فهذا وجه في الجواب عن هذه الحكاية وناهيك بقائله أبى بكر البيهقي فقد كان من أهل الرواية أيضا عن والدراية ، وتحتمل وجهاً آخر وهو أن يكون المراد بها أن يقتصر على علم یعنی الكلام ويترك تعلم الفقه ، الذى يتوصل به إلى معرفة الحلال والحرام ، ويرفض العمل بما أمر بفعله من شرائع الإسلام ، ولا يلتزم فعل ما أمر به الشارع وترك ما نهى عنه من الأحكام ، وقد بلغني عن حاتم بن عنوان لأصم وكان من أفاضل الزهاد وأهل العلم أنه قال الكلام أصل الدين والفقه فرعه والعمل ثمره فمن اكتفى بالكلام دون الفقه والعمل تزندق ومن اكتفى بالعمل دون الكلام والفقه ابتدع ومن اكتفى بالفقه دون الكلام والعمل تفسق ، ومن تفنن فى الأبواب كلها تخلص . وقد روى مثل قول خاتم الأصم عن بعض أهل العلم أخبرناه الشيخ أبو القسم زاهر بن طاهر . المعدل ، قال أنا أبو بكر أحمد بن الحسين الحافظ قال سمعت السلمي أبا عبد الرحمن يقول ، سمعت أبا بكر الرازي يقول سمعت غيلان السمرقندى يقول سمعت أبا بكر الوراق يقول من اكتفى بالكلام من العمل دون الزهد والفقه تزندق ، ومن اكتفى بالزهد دون الفقه والكلام ابتدع ومن اكتفى بالفقه دون الزهد والورع تفسق ، ومن تفنن في الأمور كلها تخلص.
The shaykh Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Isma'il ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Farisi informed us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn ibn Ali al-Bayhaqi told us, he said: Abu Sa'd Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Malini told us H, and the shaykh Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Ahmad al-Samarqandi informed us, he said: Abu al-Qasim Isma'il ibn Mas'ada al-Jurjani informed us, he said: Abu al-Qasim Hamza ibn Yusuf al-Sahmi told us, they said: Abu Ahmad ibn Adi informed us, he said: Ja'far ibn Muhammad ibn al-Hasan ibn al-Mustafad al-Firyabi narrated to us, he said: Bishr ibn al-Walid narrated to me, he said: I heard Abu Yusuf say: Whoever seeks religion through kalam becomes a zindiq. And al-Sahmi said: And whoever seeks strange hadith lies, and whoever seeks wealth through alchemy [becomes bankrupt]. Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi said: And Malik ibn Anas narrated this; he said: And he meant, and Allah knows best, by 'kalam' the speech of the people of innovation, for in their era, only the people of innovation were known for kalam. As for Ahl al-Sunnah, they rarely engaged in kalam until they were compelled to do so later. This is one aspect in answer to this story, and sufficient is its author, Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi, for he was among the people of transmission and knowledge. And it admits another aspect: that what is meant is that one restricts himself to the science of kalam and leaves learning fiqh, by which one comes to know the halal and haram, and abandons action upon what is commanded of the laws of Islam, and does not commit to doing what the Lawgiver commanded and abandoning what He prohibited. And it has reached me from Hatim ibn 'Unwan al-Asamm, who was among the most virtuous of ascetics and scholars, that he said: Kalam is the root of the religion, fiqh is its branch, and action is its fruit. Whoever is content with kalam without fiqh and action becomes a zindiq; whoever is content with action without kalam and fiqh innovates; whoever is content with fiqh without kalam and action becomes a transgressor; and whoever masters all the categories is delivered. And a saying similar to that of Hatim al-Asamm has been narrated from some scholars. The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Zahir ibn Tahir al-Mu'addil informed us, he said: Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn al-Husayn al-Hafiz told us, he said: I heard al-Sulami Abu Abd al-Rahman say, I heard Abu Bakr al-Razi say, I heard Ghaylan al-Samarqandi say, I heard Abu Bakr al-Warraq say: Whoever is content with kalam without action, zuhd, and fiqh becomes a zindiq; whoever is content with zuhd without fiqh and kalam innovates; whoever is content with fiqh without zuhd and piety becomes a transgressor; and whoever masters all matters is delivered.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage provides al-Bayhaqi's defense against the objection. It first gives a chain of transmission for the saying of Abu Yusuf, then al-Bayhaqi offers two interpretations. The first: The 'kalam' condemned refers specifically to the speech of innovators, because in the time of Abu Yusuf and Malik, only innovators were known for kalam; Ahl al-Sunnah rarely engaged in it until later when necessity arose. This is a strong answer, and al-Bayhaqi is qualified as a transmitter and scholar. The second interpretation: The condemnation means that one restricts himself to kalam and neglects learning fiqh (jurisprudence) and abandoning action upon Islamic laws. To support this, the author cites Hatim al-Asamm's classification: kalam is the root, fiqh the branch, action the fruit; neglecting any leads to zandaqah, innovation, or transgression. Then a similar saying from Abu Bakr al-Warraq emphasizes the interdependence of kalam, zuhd, and fiqh. The passage thus defends kalam by clarifying that the blame is directed at those who misuse it or neglect other obligations, not at kalam itself.

أهل السنة
الفقه
الزهد
العمل
تزندق
ابتدع
تفسق

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All engagement in kalam (theological discourse) is forbidden based on early statements.
Correction: Al-Bayhaqi clarifies that the condemnation was directed at the kalam of innovators, or at those who neglect fiqh and action, not at all kalam.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bayhaqi's first interpretation, what kind of kalam is being condemned in the narration?
A) The kalam of Ahl al-Sunnah
B) The kalam of the people of innovation
C) All kalam without exception
D) The kalam of the Sufis

Key Takeaway
Al-Bayhaqi defends kalam by showing that the condemnation applies only to the kalam of innovators or to those who abandon fiqh and action, not to balanced theological inquiry.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content with learning about Allah (kalam) while neglecting to learn the rulings of halal and haram (fiqh)? How does Hatim's warning that such a person becomes a zindiq make you feel about your own studies? What will you change?
?
Do you prioritize strict asceticism (zuhd) or abundant action over sound theology (kalam)? The saying of Abu Bakr al-Warraq warns that neglecting kalam leads to innovation. Is there an area of your practice that lacks theological grounding? What step will you take today to fix that?
?
This passage teaches that mastery of all categories—kalam, fiqh, and action—is necessary for deliverance. Which of these three is weakest in your current pursuit of knowledge, and what practical step will you take this week to strengthen it?

Al-Shafi'i on the Endlessness of Kalam and the Danger of Takfir
Anecdote of al-Shafi'i and al-Bayhaqi's explanation of his avoidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Shafi'i, despite mastering kalam, chose to avoid debating it, and the principle that some errors can lead to accusations of disbelief.

Core Idea
Kalam has no end, and an error in it can be fatal to one's faith.

This lesson presents a famous anecdote about Imam al-Shafi'i. While others debated at his door, he remained silent for seven days. When he emerged, he explained that he had mastered kalam but chose to abandon it because unlike other disciplines, a mistake in kalam could lead to being declared a disbeliever. The lesson also shows that al-Shafi'i's avoidance was not due to ignorance but wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the anecdote and its interpretation
Read the anecdote where al-Shafi'i overhears people debating kalam, then al-Bayhaqi's immediate explanation that al-Shafi'i had mastered it.
2
Compare archery and kalam
Notice al-Shafi'i's analogy: in archery, a miss is just a miss; in kalam, an error is takfir.
This highlights the high stakes of theological debate.
3
Reflect on the wisdom of avoidance
Consider why even a capable scholar like al-Shafi'i would avoid kalam – not due to ignorance, but due to the endlessness and risk.
This echoes the Salaf's cautious approach.

دخلت فيه حتى بلغت منه مبلغا وما تعاطيت شيئا إلا وبلغت فيه مبلغاً ، حتى الرمي كنت أرمى بين الغرضين فأصيب من عشرة تسعة ولكن الكلام لا غاية له ، تناظروا في شيء إن أخطأتم فيه يقال لكم أخطأتم لا تناظروا فى ملكوت السموات والأرض شيء إلا بحكم الله وتقديره وإرادته وكذلك في سائر مسائل الكلام اكتفوا بما فيهما من الدلالة على صحة قولهم حتى طائفة سموا ما في كتاب الله من الحجة عليهم متشابها ، وقالوا نترك القول بالاخبار أصلا وزعموا أن الأخبار التي حملت عليهم لا تصح في عقولهم فقام جماعة من أئمتنا رحمهم الله بهذا العلم وبينوا لمن وفق للصواب ورزق الفهم أن جميع ما ورد في تلك الأخبار صحيح في العقول وما أدعوه في الكتاب من التشابه باطل في العقول وحين أظهروا بدعهم وذكروا ما اغتر به أهل الضعف من شبههم أجابوه فكشفوا عنها بما هو حجة عندهم كما فعل الشافعي فيما حكينا عنه لوجوب الامر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر ، وما والله أعلم بقوله يعنى من ارتدى بالكلام ، لم يفلح كلام أهل الأهواء الذين تركوا الكتاب والسنة وجعلوا معولهم عقولهم وأخذوا في تسوية الكتاب عليها ، وحين حملت عليهم السنة بزيادة بيان لنقض أقاويلهم أتهموا As for his [al-Shafi'i's] preference for refraining from delving into it and turning away from debate about it despite his knowledge of it: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, he said: I heard Abu al-Fadl al-Hasan ibn Ya'qub al-'Adl say: I heard Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Ruh say: We were at the door of al-Shafi'i debating about kalam. Then al-Shafi'i came out to us and heard some of what we were in, then he went back from us. He did not come out to us until after seven days. Then he came out and said: 'Nothing prevented me from coming out to you except an ailment that occurred, but when I heard you debating about it, do you think that I am not good at it? I indeed entered into it until I reached a high level in it, and I never undertook anything except that I reached a high level in it, even archery: I used to shoot between two targets and hit nine out of ten. But kalam has no end. Debate about something that if you err in it, it is said to you: You erred. Do not debate about something that if you err in it, it is said to you: You disbelieved.' Al-Bayhaqi said: And in the narration of al-Muzani from al-Shafi'i is evidence that he had learned kalam and excelled in it, then he preferred to abandon debate about it when there was no need for it. He only censured the doctrine of the Qadariyya. Do you not see that he said 'with something of these whims' and he preferred to abandon argument about it? And it seems he followed what we narrated from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Do not sit with the people of qadr (predestination deniers) and do not initiate discussion with them'—the hadith or other reports narrated in its meaning. And upon that our imams proceeded in ancient times when there was no need for kalam about it. When they needed it, they answered with what is in the Book of Allah, then in the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, of evidence for establishing qadr (divine decree) of Allah Most High, and that nothing occurs in the dominion of the heavens and the earth except by Allah's judgment, determination, and will. Likewise in all other questions of kalam, they sufficed with what is in both of them of evidence for the correctness of their statement, until a group called what is in the Book of Allah of proof against them 'mutashabih' (ambiguous), and they said: We abandon speaking about the reports entirely, and they claimed that the reports that were brought against them are not valid in their intellects. So a group of our imams (may Allah have mercy on them) stood up for this knowledge and explained to those who were guided to correctness and granted understanding that all that came in those reports is sound in the intellects, and what they claim of ambiguity in the Book is false in the intellects. And when they manifested their innovations and mentioned what the weak people were deceived by of their specious arguments, they answered them, exposing them with what is a proof according to them, as al-Shafi'i did in what we narrated from him, due to the obligation of commanding the good and forbidding the evil. And what is in abandoning the forbidding of evil and being silent about it of corruption and transgression. And in ancient times, they were only known by 'kalam' as the people of whims. As for Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, their reliance in what they believe is the Book and the Sunnah, so they were not named by their name. And by his statement, 'whoever dons kalam (i.e., makes it his garment), he will not succeed,' he means, and Allah knows best, the speech of the people of whims who abandoned the Book and the Sunnah and made their intellects their reliance and took to leveling the Book upon them. And when the Sunnah was brought against them with additional clarification to refute their sayings, they accused its narrators and turned away from it. As for Ahl al-Sunna, their method in the fundamentals is founded...
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage consists of a second anecdote followed by a lengthy commentary from al-Bayhaqi. The anecdote: A group of people were debating kalam at al-Shafi'i's door. He overheard them, went back inside, and did not come out for seven days. When he emerged, he explained that he had mastered many arts, including archery (hitting nine out of ten), and likewise he had mastered kalam. However, kalam has no end—unlike archery, where you can miss and simply be told you erred, in kalam an error leads to accusations of disbelief (kufr). Therefore, he avoided it. Al-Bayhaqi then interprets this: al-Shafi'i's avoidance was not due to ignorance but because he knew it deeply and chose to leave it when not needed. He specifically censured the Qadariyya (those who deny predestination) and followed the prophetic command not to debate them. Al-Bayhaqi then describes the method of the early imams (Ahl al-Sunna): they relied on the Book and Sunnah, and when attacked by heretics, they responded with rational proofs from revelation. A group of innovators claimed that some Quranic verses were ambiguous (mutashabih) and rejected hadiths that contradicted them. The imams defended the authenticity of the reports and showed that they are sound in reason. They exposed the heretics' arguments as part of 'commanding good and forbidding evil'. The passage concludes by distinguishing Ahl al-Sunna from the people of whims: the former base their creed entirely on the Book and Sunnah, not on their intellects overriding revelation. The final sentence is cut off, but it states that Ahl al-Sunna's method in fundamentals is founded (on the Book and Sunnah).

Key Terms
الكلام
الجدال
التكفير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Shafi'i avoided kalam because he was not skilled in it.
Correction: Al-Shafi'i explicitly says he reached a high level in kalam and even mastered archery; his avoidance was due to the risk of takfir and endlessness, not ignorance.

Checkpoint
What was al-Shafi'i's main reason for avoiding debate in kalam, according to this passage?
A) He was not good at it
B) It has no end and error leads to accusations of disbelief
C) It is forbidden under all circumstances
D) He was too busy with archery

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Shafi'i's example teaches that even if one is capable in kalam, it may be wiser to avoid debates that risk faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in arguments about religion, do you consciously acknowledge that an error could be fatal to your faith, or do you treat it like a harmless intellectual game?
?
Al-Shafi'i had mastered kalam yet chose to walk away. Is there an argument or debate you are currently clinging to out of pride, even though it leads you into dangerous territory?
?
What would it cost you today to stop one pointless religious debate that has no end and only risks your iman? Can you accept that cost for the sake of your faith?

The Salaf's Method: Reliance on Revelation and Refutation of Innovators
Al-Bayhaqi's commentary on the Salaf's method and refutation of heretics.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the methodology of Ahl al-Sunna in defending creed: relying on Quran and Sunnah with rational proofs while avoiding endless speculation.

Core Idea
Ahl al-Sunna base their creed on revelation, not on intellect overriding it.

After explaining al-Shafi'i's personal stance, al-Bayhaqi outlines the broader approach of the Salaf. When necessary, they used rational arguments grounded in scripture. They refuted heretics who claimed Quranic verses were ambiguous and rejected hadiths. This lesson explains their method and how it differs from the people of whims.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Bayhaqi's description of the imams' response
Read how the early imams answered heretics using evidence from the Book and Sunnah when needed.
2
Identify the innovators' tactic
Notice the group that called Quranic proofs 'mutashabih' and rejected hadiths as intellectually invalid.
This is a common strategy to avoid accepting revelation.
3
Understand the imams' defense
The imams proved that the reports are sound in reason and that the claim of ambiguity is false, fulfilling the duty of commanding good.
4
Distinguish Ahl al-Sunna from people of whims
Al-Bayhaqi ends by contrasting the two: Ahl al-Sunna rely on scripture, while people of whims rely on intellect and accuse narrators.
This clarifies the correct methodology.

Source Text

فأما استحبابه ترك الخوض فيه والإعراض عن المناظرة فيه مع معرفته به فاخبرنا أبو عبد الله الحافظ ، قال سمعت أبا الفضل الحسن ابن يعقوب العدل يقول سمعت أبا أحمد محمد بن روح ، يقول كنا على باب الشافعي ( بشيء من هذه الأهواء ( واستحب ترك الجدال فيه وكأنه تبع ما رويناه عن عمر بن الخطاب عن النبي أنه قال : لا تجالسوا أهل القدر ولا تفاتحوهم الحديث أو غير ذلك من الاخبار الواردة في معناه وعلى مثل ذلك جرى أئمتنا في قديم الدهر عند الاستغناء عن الكلام فيه ، فإذا احتاجوا إليه أجابوا بما في كتاب الله عز وجل ، ثم في سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم من الدلالة على إثبات القدر الله عز وجل وأنه لا يجرى في ملكوت السموات والأرض شيء إلا بحكم الله وتقديره وإرادته وكذلك في سائر مسائل الكلام اكتفوا بما فيهما من الدلالة على صحة قولهم حتى طائفة سموا ما في كتاب الله من الحجة عليهم متشابها ، وقالوا نترك القول بالاخبار أصلا وزعموا أن الأخبار التي حملت عليهم لا تصح في عقولهم فقام جماعة من أئمتنا رحمهم الله بهذا العلم وبينوا لمن وفق للصواب ورزق الفهم أن جميع ما ورد في تلك الأخبار صحيح في العقول وما أدعوه في الكتاب من التشابه باطل في العقول وحين أظهروا بدعهم وذكروا ما اغتر به أهل الضعف من شبههم أجابوه فكشفوا عنها بما هو حجة عندهم كما فعل الشافعي فيما حكينا عنه لوجوب الامر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر ، وما في ترك إنكار المنكر والسكوت عليه من الفساد والتـعـدى وكانوا فى القديم إنما يعرفون بالكلام أهل الأهواء، فأما أهل السنة والجماعة فمعولهم فيما يعتقدون الكتاب والسنة فكانوا لا يسمون بتسميتهم وإنما یعنى والله أعلم بقوله يعنى من ارتدى بالكلام ، لم يفلح كلام أهل الأهواء الذين تركوا الكتاب والسنة وجعلوا معولهم عقولهم وأخذوا في تسوية الكتاب عليها ، وحين حملت عليهم السنة بزيادة بيان لنقض أقاويلهم أتهموا رواتها وأعرضوا عنها ، فأما أهل السنة فمذهبهم في الأصول مبنى
As for his [al-Shafi'i's] preference for refraining from delving into it and turning away from debate about it despite his knowledge of it: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, he said: I heard Abu al-Fadl al-Hasan ibn Ya'qub al-'Adl say: I heard Abu Ahmad Muhammad ibn Ruh say: We were at the door of al-Shafi'i debating about kalam. Then al-Shafi'i came out to us and heard some of what we were in, then he went back from us. He did not come out to us until after seven days. Then he came out and said: 'Nothing prevented me from coming out to you except an ailment that occurred, but when I heard you debating about it, do you think that I am not good at it? I indeed entered into it until I reached a high level in it, and I never undertook anything except that I reached a high level in it, even archery: I used to shoot between two targets and hit nine out of ten. But kalam has no end. Debate about something that if you err in it, it is said to you: You erred. Do not debate about something that if you err in it, it is said to you: You disbelieved.' Al-Bayhaqi said: And in the narration of al-Muzani from al-Shafi'i is evidence that he had learned kalam and excelled in it, then he preferred to abandon debate about it when there was no need for it. He only censured the doctrine of the Qadariyya. Do you not see that he said 'with something of these whims' and he preferred to abandon argument about it? And it seems he followed what we narrated from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Do not sit with the people of qadr (predestination deniers) and do not initiate discussion with them'—the hadith or other reports narrated in its meaning. And upon that our imams proceeded in ancient times when there was no need for kalam about it. When they needed it, they answered with what is in the Book of Allah, then in the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah, of evidence for establishing qadr (divine decree) of Allah Most High, and that nothing occurs in the dominion of the heavens and the earth except by Allah's judgment, determination, and will. Likewise in all other questions of kalam, they sufficed with what is in both of them of evidence for the correctness of their statement, until a group called what is in the Book of Allah of proof against them 'mutashabih' (ambiguous), and they said: We abandon speaking about the reports entirely, and they claimed that the reports that were brought against them are not valid in their intellects. So a group of our imams (may Allah have mercy on them) stood up for this knowledge and explained to those who were guided to correctness and granted understanding that all that came in those reports is sound in the intellects, and what they claim of ambiguity in the Book is false in the intellects. And when they manifested their innovations and mentioned what the weak people were deceived by of their specious arguments, they answered them, exposing them with what is a proof according to them, as al-Shafi'i did in what we narrated from him, due to the obligation of commanding the good and forbidding the evil. And what is in abandoning the forbidding of evil and being silent about it of corruption and transgression. And in ancient times, they were only known by 'kalam' as the people of whims. As for Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, their reliance in what they believe is the Book and the Sunnah, so they were not named by their name. And by his statement, 'whoever dons kalam (i.e., makes it his garment), he will not succeed,' he means, and Allah knows best, the speech of the people of whims who abandoned the Book and the Sunnah and made their intellects their reliance and took to leveling the Book upon them. And when the Sunnah was brought against them with additional clarification to refute their sayings, they accused its narrators and turned away from it. As for Ahl al-Sunna, their method in the fundamentals is founded...
Source pages p. 257

Commentary
This passage consists of a second anecdote followed by a lengthy commentary from al-Bayhaqi. The anecdote: A group of people were debating kalam at al-Shafi'i's door. He overheard them, went back inside, and did not come out for seven days. When he emerged, he explained that he had mastered many arts, including archery (hitting nine out of ten), and likewise he had mastered kalam. However, kalam has no end—unlike archery, where you can miss and simply be told you erred, in kalam an error leads to accusations of disbelief (kufr). Therefore, he avoided it. Al-Bayhaqi then interprets this: al-Shafi'i's avoidance was not due to ignorance but because he knew it deeply and chose to leave it when not needed. He specifically censured the Qadariyya (those who deny predestination) and followed the prophetic command not to debate them. Al-Bayhaqi then describes the method of the early imams (Ahl al-Sunna): they relied on the Book and Sunnah, and when attacked by heretics, they responded with rational proofs from revelation. A group of innovators claimed that some Quranic verses were ambiguous (mutashabih) and rejected hadiths that contradicted them. The imams defended the authenticity of the reports and showed that they are sound in reason. They exposed the heretics' arguments as part of 'commanding good and forbidding evil'. The passage concludes by distinguishing Ahl al-Sunna from the people of whims: the former base their creed entirely on the Book and Sunnah, not on their intellects overriding revelation. The final sentence is cut off, but it states that Ahl al-Sunna's method in fundamentals is founded (on the Book and Sunnah).

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
أهل الأهواء
المتشابه
الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ahl al-Sunna never use rational arguments.
Correction: They use rational arguments grounded in the Book and Sunnah when necessary, as shown in this passage.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bayhaqi, what did the early imams do when they needed to respond to heretics?
A) They ignored them
B) They answered using evidence from the Book and Sunnah
C) They debated endlessly
D) They relied solely on intellect

Key Takeaway
The Salaf's method was to ground all arguments in revelation, and they only engaged in kalam when necessary to defend the truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a religious argument that unsettles you, do you instinctively rely on your own reasoning or do you turn to the Quran and Sunnah? Which path are you following: that of the Salaf or of the people of whims?
?
Have you ever dismissed a clear proof from the Book or Sunnah by thinking 'this is too ambiguous' or 'this doesn't make sense to me'? What does that reveal about your trust in revelation over your intellect?
?
The Salaf only engaged in refutation when it was an obligation. Are you quick to argue and correct others, or do you weigh whether it is truly necessary for commanding good and forbidding evil? Examine your motives: are they for truth or for your own ego?

Al-Bayhaqi on the Reasons for Al-Shafi'i's Prohibition of Kalam
Al-Bayhaqi explains why al-Shafi'i forbade engagement in kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical and practical reasons behind al-Shafi'i's discouragement of kalam, as explained by al-Bayhaqi.

Core Idea
Al-Shafi'i's ban on kalam was a protective measure, not a doctrinal rejection.

Al-Bayhaqi provides a nuanced historical account of why al-Shafi'i and other early imams advised against engaging in kalam. This passage reveals that the prohibition was not absolute but a response to the political and religious climate of the time, where kalam debates could lead to persecution. Let's examine the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Understand the historical context
Learn about al-Shafi'i's encounters with al-Ma'mun's court, including his observations of Bishr al-Marisi and other innovators.
This sets the stage for why al-Shafi'i acted as he did.
2
Identify the key reasons for prohibition
Note the specific observations al-Shafi'i made: the dominance of innovators, the foresight of the mihna, and the dislike of associating with rulers.
These reasons are intertwined and all point to protecting the scholars.
3
Grasp the precautionary nature
Understand that al-Shafi'i's instruction to avoid kalam was to prevent his companions from being drawn into debates that could lead to their persecution.
This shows the prohibition was practical, not doctrinal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال البيهقي ولاستحباب الشافعي ومن كان في عصره من أئمتنا ترك الخوض في الكلام وترك الاشتهار به عند الاستغناء عنه معنى آخر ، وهو أن الشافعي حين قدم العراق في خلافة الرشيد كان قد دخل على المأمون باستدعائه دخوله عليه ورأى تقريبه بشرا المريسى وأمثاله من أهل البدع ، وحين عاد إلى العراق في خلافة المأمون شاهد غلبة أهل الأهواء على مجلسه وأحس ببعض ما رأى أهل السنة من غلبة أهل الأهواء في عصره ثم بما أصابهم من المحنة في أيام المعتصم والواثق فحين شاهد الشافعي أمثال ذلك وأحس ببعض ما كان وراء ذلك مع كراهيته وكراهية من أهل الورع الدخول على السلاطين والاختلاط بهم لأصحابه ترك الخوض فيه لئلا يدعوا إلى مجالستهم للمناظرة فيه ولئلا يكون ذلك سببا لمحنتهم
Al-Bayhaqi said: And the recommendation of al-Shafi'i and those of our imams in his time to avoid engagement in kalam and avoid being known for it when there is no need for it has another meaning, which is that al-Shafi'i when he came to Iraq in the caliphate of al-Rashid, he had entered upon al-Ma'mun at his request and saw him bringing close Bishr al-Marisi and his likes from among the people of innovation, and when he returned to Iraq in the caliphate of al-Ma'mun, he witnessed the dominance of the people of desires in his assembly and sensed some of what the people of the Sunnah saw of the dominance of the people of desires in his time, then what befell them of the trial in the days of al-Mu'tasim and al-Wathiq. So when al-Shafi'i witnessed such things and sensed some of what was behind that, with his disapproval and the disapproval of the pious of entering upon the rulers and mixing with them for his companions, he avoided engagement in it lest they be invited to their gatherings for debate and lest that be a cause for their trial.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is an explanation by al-Bayhaqi of the reason behind al-Shafi'i's and other early imams' discouragement of engaging in kalam. Al-Bayhaqi begins by stating that there is another meaning (beyond the obvious) for their recommendation to avoid kalam and not to be known for it when there is no need. He provides the historical context: when al-Shafi'i first came to Iraq during al-Rashid's caliphate, he saw that al-Ma'mun (then crown prince) had brought Bishr al-Marisi and other innovators close to him. When he returned to Iraq later during al-Ma'mun's caliphate, he witnessed the dominance of the people of desires (innovators) in the caliph's assembly and sensed the persecution (mihna) that would later befall the scholars under al-Mu'tasim and al-Wathiq. Because of these observations, and because he himself disliked entering upon rulers and mixing with them, he ordered his companions to avoid kalam so that they would not be invited to debate in the rulers' gatherings, which could lead to their persecution. Thus, the prohibition was not due to any weakness in kalam itself, but as a practical measure to protect the scholars.

Key Terms
الخوض في الكلام
أهل الأهواء
المحنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Shafi'i forbade kalam because debate is inherently wrong.
Correction: Al-Bayhaqi clarifies that the prohibition was a practical measure to protect scholars from persecution due to the political climate, not because kalam itself is invalid.

Checkpoint
According to al-Bayhaqi, what did al-Shafi'i observe in al-Ma'mun's court that contributed to his forbidding kalam?
A) The caliph's love for debate
B) The presence of innovators like Bishr al-Marisi
C) The caliph's persecution of scholars
D) The weakness of his companions

Key Takeaway
Al-Shafi'i's prohibition of kalam was a context-sensitive precaution to protect scholars from persecution, not a universal condemnation of theological discourse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When have you avoided a religious discussion or debate because of fear of what others might think or do to you? Was that avoidance truly wise, or just comfortable?
?
Al-Shafi'i adjusted his advice based on the political climate. Where in your life have you mistaken a temporary precaution for an eternal ruling, applying it rigidly without considering context?
?
This lesson shows that even great scholars feared the harm of mixing with rulers. Is your own religious practice ever influenced by a desire to be accepted by those in power? What would it cost you to be truthful regardless of the audience?

The Salaf and the Proofs of Faith
Ibn Asakir refutes the claim that the Salaf neglected usul al-din and explains why they didn't write formal proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Salaf's lack of written works on kalam does not indicate ignorance, but rather reflects their unique historical context where the truths of faith were self-evident.

Core Idea
The Salaf knew the proofs of faith intimately; they just didn't need to write them down.

Ibn Asakir responds to a common accusation that the early Muslims neglected the foundations of religion (usul al-din). He argues that such a claim is both irrational and religiously offensive, given their expertise in intricate legal matters. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the historical context that explains their approach.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the rhetorical force and the structure: a refutation followed by a positive explanation.
The passage ends abruptly; the argument is complete in its core.
2
Identify the accusation and its refutation
Find where Ibn Asakir states the accusation that the Salaf forbade or neglected knowledge of usul. Then see how he refutes it by pointing to their expertise in detailed fiqh issues, making it rationally and religiously impossible that they would be ignorant of the greatest matter.
The key phrase is 'يستحيل في العقل والدين' — it is impossible rationally and religiously.
3
Understand the historical explanation
Ibn Asakir explains why the Salaf did not formulate elaborate proofs: they lived when the Sharia was fresh, they witnessed the Prophet's miracles, and the truths were obvious through revelation and natural intellect. They were independent of formal argumentation.
The phrase 'ببدائه العقول' refers to clear intellectual proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرني الشيخ أبو القسم نصر بن نصر الواعظ في كتابه عن القاضي أبي المعالي بن عبد الملك: اعتقد أن السلف الصالح رضي عنهم نهوا عن معرفة الأصول وتجنبوها أو تغافلوا عنها وأهملوها فقد اعتقد فيهم عجزا وأساء بهم ظنا لأنه يستحيل في العقل والدين عند كل من أنصف من نفسه أن الواحد منهم يتكلم في مسألة العول وقضايا الجد وكمية الحدود وكيفية القصاص بفصول ويباهل عليها ويلاحن ويجاثي فيها ويبالغ ويذكر في إزالة النجاسات عشرين دليلا لنفسه وللمخالف ويشقق الشعر في النظر فيها ثم لا يعرف ربه الأمر خلقه بالتحليل والتحريم والمكلف عباده للترك والتعظيم. فهيهات أن يكون ذلك. وإنما أهملوا تحرير أدلته وإقرار أسئلته وأجوبته، فإن الله سبحانه وتعالى بعث نبينا محمدا صلوات الله عليه وسلامه فأيده بالآيات الباهرة والمعجزات القاهرة، حتى أوضح الشريعة وبينها وعلمهم مواقيتها وعينها فلم يترك لهم أصلا من الأصول إلا بناه وشيده، ولا حكما من الأحكام إلا أوضحه ومهده لقوله سبحانه وتعالى: {وأنزلنا إليك الذكر لتبين للناس ما نزل إليهم ولعلهم يتفكرون} فاطمأنت قلوب الصحابة لما عاينوا من عجائب الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم وشاهدوا من صدق التنزيل ببدائه العقول، والشريعة غضة طرية متداولة بينهم في مواسمهم ومجالسهم يعرفون التوحيد مشاهدة بالوحي والسماع، ويتكلمون في أدلة الوحدانية بالطباع مستغنين عن تحرير أدلتها وتقويم
The shaykh Abu al-Qasim Nasr ibn Nasr al-Wa'iz informed me in his book from the qadi Abu al-Ma'ali ibn Abd al-Malik: To believe that the righteous Salaf, may Allah be pleased with them, forbade the knowledge of the foundations (usul) and shunned them, or were negligent of them and abandoned them, is to believe in their incapacity and to think badly of them. For it is impossible, rationally and religiously, according to anyone who is fair to himself, that one of them would speak about the issue of al-awl and the cases of the grandfather, the quantities of the hudud, the modality of qisas with details, and argue over them, engage in debate, contend, exaggerate, mention twenty proofs for himself and for the opponent, split hairs in examining them, and then not know his Lord who commanded His creation with analysis and prohibition, and charged His servants with abandonment and veneration. Far be it from that! Rather, they neglected to formulate its proofs and to establish its questions and answers because Allah, Exalted and High, sent our Prophet Muhammad, blessings and peace upon him, and supported him with dazzling signs and overwhelming miracles, until he clarified the Sharia and explained it, and taught them its timings and specified them, leaving no foundation from the foundations except that he built and reinforced it, and no ruling from the rulings except that he clarified and paved it, due to His saying, Exalted and High: {And We sent down to you the Reminder that you may make clear to the people what was sent down to them, and that they might reflect.} So the hearts of the Companions were at ease because of what they beheld of the wonders of the Messenger and witnessed of the truth of the revelation with the intellect's clear proofs, and the Sharia was fresh and new, circulated among them in their seasons and gatherings; they knew tawhid by direct witnessing through revelation and hearing, and they spoke about the proofs of oneness by natural disposition, independent of formulating its proofs and straightening
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the accusation that the Salaf neglected the science of usul al-din (the foundations of religion, i.e., kalam). The author argues that it is logically and religiously impossible that the Salaf, who rigorously debated intricate fiqh issues like 'awl (inheritance shares), grandfather cases, hudud punishments, and qisas, detailed rulings on removing impurities with multiple proofs, and engaged in intense scholarly debates, would be ignorant of the greatest matter: knowing Allah and His commands. To claim they abandoned kalam is to think ill of them. The author then explains why the Salaf did not elaborate proofs: because they lived in the immediate aftermath of revelation, witnessing the Prophet's miracles and the Quran's clarity. The Sharia was fresh and evident; they knew tawhid through direct experience of revelation and natural disposition. Therefore, they did not need to formulate extensive arguments. This defends the legitimacy of later kalam while honoring the Salaf's unique position.

Key Terms
السلف الصالح
الأصول
تحرير الأدلة
الآيات الباهرة
بدائه العقول
أدلة الوحدانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Salaf were ignorant of theology and forbade its study.
Correction: The Salaf had deep knowledge of usul al-din but did not need to write formal proofs because the truth was evident through revelation and miracles in their time.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Asakir, why did the Salaf not formulate elaborate proofs for usul al-din?
A) They were incapable of doing so.
B) They considered kalam forbidden.
C) The proofs were so obvious from revelation and miracles that they did not need elaboration.
D) They relied solely on Greek philosophy.

Key Takeaway
The Salaf's deep knowledge of the foundations of faith was intuitive and immediate due to their direct encounter with revelation, not absent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever doubted your faith because you couldn't articulate a 'proof' the way kalam scholars do? How does the direct certainty of the Salaf challenge your reliance on formal arguments? Will you seek to strengthen your conviction by immersing in the Quran and Sunnah as they did, rather than only intellectual proofs?
?
When you encounter debates about the foundations of deen, do you feel inadequate if you lack a systematic theological response? This lesson says the Salaf didn't need that. What is the state of your heart regarding the truths of faith — is it alive through contemplation of revelation, or have you outsourced certainty to borrowed arguments? Decide one concrete step to make the Quran and Sunnah your primary source of certainty this week.
?
The Salaf debated fiqh with twenty proofs but rested securely in tawhid without writing them down. Are you more concerned with defending secondary issues than with nurturing your direct relationship with Allah? What would change if you devoted the same energy you spend on argumentation to reflecting on the signs of Allah in His creation and revelation?

The Historical Precedent for Codifying Kalam
Ibn Asakir argues that kalam is not an innovation by analogy with other sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ibn Asakir argues that the science of kalam is not an innovation, using an analogy with the codification of other Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Kalam is not an innovation; it follows the pattern of grammar and tafsir.

This passage from Ibn Asakir’s work addresses a common accusation against kalam: that it is a bid‘ah (innovation) because it uses technical reasoning not found in the early generations. Ibn Asakir counters by pointing out that other sciences like grammar, tafsir, and hadith classification were also compiled later, yet no one called them innovations. His argument sets the stage for accepting kalam as a legitimate discipline.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read Ibn Asakir's original Arabic and the literal English translation. Notice the flow of his argument from the earlier generations to later necessities.
The Arabic may have some ambiguous phrases due to OCR; rely on the translation for clarity.
2
Identify the historical steps
Ibn Asakir describes two eras: the early generations who knew sciences without codification, and later generations who faced challenges and compiled them. List the challenges they faced and the sciences they compiled.
Look for words like 'then when their era ended' and 'so they were compelled'.
3
Understand the analogy
Why does Ibn Asakir mention grammar, tafsir, etc.? He argues that if those compilations were not innovations, then compiling kalam is also not an innovation. Reflect on how this analogy defends kalam.
The key line is 'And no one said that all of these were innovations...'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حجتها وعللها كما أنهم كانوا يعرفون تفسير القرآن ، ومعانى الشعر والبيان وترتيب النحو والعروض ، وفتاوى النوافل والفروض من غير تحرير العلة ولا تقويم الأدلة ، ثم لما انقرضت أيامهم وتغيرت طباع من بعدهم وكلامهم ، وخالطهم من غير جنسهم ، وطال بالسلف الصالح والعرب العرباء عهدهم، أشكل عليهم تفسير القرآن ومرن عليهم غلط اللسان ، وكثر المخالفون في الاصول والفروع ، واضطروا إلى جمع العروض والنحو وتمييز المراسيل من المسانيد والآحاد عن التواتر ، وصنفوا التفسير والتعليق وبينوا التدقيق والتحقيق، ولم يقل قائل أن هذه كلها بدع ظهرت أو أنها محالات جمعت ودونت ، بل هو الشرع الصحيح والرأى الصريح
Their proofs and causes, just as they used to know the interpretation of the Quran, the meanings of poetry and eloquence, the ordering of grammar and prosody, and the legal rulings of supererogatory and obligatory acts without formulating the cause nor establishing the proofs. Then when their era ended, the dispositions of those after them and their speech changed, and they mixed with those not of their kind, and the covenant became distant from the righteous predecessors and the pure Arabs. The interpretation of the Quran became difficult for them, and errors of the tongue became common, and the opponents in principles and branches increased. So they were compelled to compile prosody and grammar, to distinguish the mursal from the musnad, and the solitary from the mutawatir, and they authored tafsir and commentary, and clarified precision and verification. And no one said that all of these were innovations that appeared or impossibilities collected and recorded. Rather, it is the correct Shariah and the explicit opinion.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an argument by analogy defending the science of kalam against the charge of innovation. Ibn Asakir first describes the earlier generations: they had direct knowledge of Quranic exegesis, Arabic poetry, grammar, prosody, and legal rulings without needing to systematically record the underlying principles or proofs. But after that era ended, language corruption set in, non-Arabs mixed in, and the distance from the early Muslims grew. This led to confusion in understanding the Quran and increase in linguistic errors, as well as more opponents in both foundational (usul) and branch (furu') matters. Consequently, the community was compelled to formalize and write down the sciences of prosody, grammar, hadith classification (mursal vs musnad, ahad vs tawatur), tafsir, and legal commentary. Importantly, no one at that time labeled these compilations as innovations or invalid; rather, they were accepted as correct Shariah and sound reasoning. The implication is that the later formalization of kalam should be viewed in the same light.

Key Terms
بدع (innovations)
الشرع الصحيح (correct Shariah)
الرأى الصريح (explicit opinion)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that kalam is an innovation (bid‘ah) because it uses technical terms and methods not employed by the early Muslims.
Correction: Ibn Asakir shows that other sciences like grammar, tafsir, and hadith classification were also compiled later without being called innovations, so kalam is analogous and therefore not an innovation.

Checkpoint
Why does Ibn Asakir cite the codification of grammar and tafsir?
A) To show that early Muslims invented these sciences.
B) To draw an analogy: if these compilations were not bid'ah, then kalam is not either.
C) To argue that kalam is more important than grammar.
D) To prove that all later sciences are invalid.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Asakir defends kalam by showing that the formalization of knowledge is a natural response to historical circumstances, not a religious innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the early scholars had rejected all later compilations as innovations, you would not have the books of tafsir and hadith you rely on today. In what areas of your own practice might you be unknowingly rejecting a legitimate development because it was not done by the Salaf? What would it take for you to recognize it as 'correct Shariah and explicit opinion'?
?
The passage describes how errors of the tongue and confusion increased due to mixing with non-Arabs. Consider your own understanding of Islamic knowledge. Are you aware of any errors or confusions in your own beliefs that might come from not being grounded in the original sources? What steps are you taking to ensure your understanding is sound?
?
Ibn Asakir argues that necessity compelled scholars to compile sciences. Reflect on a time when you felt compelled to seek deeper knowledge due to a challenge. Did you embrace it or resist? How can you apply the lesson's principle that responding to changing circumstances is not innovation but part of the Shariah?
