Method of Learning
beginner
4 min
Dream of Ibrahim: Endorsement of Kalam
Dream of al-Juwayni with Prophet Ibrahim asking about kalam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a dream of Prophet Ibrahim endorsed the science of kalam as a tool to repel doubts and falsehoods.

Core Idea
Kalam is the weapon against doubts and falsehoods.

This lesson presents a remarkable dream witnessed by Imam al-Juwayni, in which he meets Prophet Ibrahim and asks about kalam. The Prophet's answer affirms the value of this science in defending the truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the dream narrative
Read the Arabic account of al-Juwayni's dream and see how it establishes the prophetic endorsement.
2
Analyze Ibrahim's response
Ibrahim says kalam repels doubts and falsehoods. Reflect on what this implies about the necessity of kalam.
3
Consider the significance
Why is a prophetic endorsement important for a discipline like kalam? Think about the authority it provides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخبرنا الشيخ أبو القسم عبد الرحمن بن الحسن بن أحمد الجرجاني الصوفي ، المعروف بالشعر بنيسابور ، قال سمعت أبا الحسن على بن أحمد المدينى يقول : سمعت الإمام أبا محمد عبد الله بن يوسف الجويني يقول رأيت إبراهيم الخليل عليه السلام فى المنام فأهويت لأن أقبل رجليه فمنعني من ذلك تكرماً لى فاستدبرت فقبلت عقبيه ، فأولت الرفعة والبركة تبقى في عقـبـي ، ثم قلت يا خليل الله ما تقول في علم الكلام فقال يدفع به الشبه والأباطيل. أخبرنا الشيخ الإمام أبو نصر عبد الرحيم بن عبد الكريم بن هوازن إجازة قال سئل أبي الأستاذ أبو القسم القشيري رحمه الله فقيل له أرباب التوحيد هل يتفاوتون فيه فقال أن فرقت بين مصل ل وعلمت أن هذا يصلى وقلبه مشحون بالغفلات وذاك لى وقلبه حاضر ففرق بين عالم وعالم ، هذا لو طرأت عليه مشكلة لم يمكنه الخروج منها وهذا يقاوم كل عدو للإسلام ويحل كل معضلة تعز فى مقام الخصام وهذا هو الجهاد الأكبر فإن الجهاد في الظاهر مع أقوام معينين وهذا جهاد مع جميع أعداء الدين
The Shaykh Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Hasan ibn Ahmad al-Jurjani al-Sufi, known as al-Shi'r in Nishapur, informed us, saying: I heard Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad al-Madini say: I heard Imam Abu Muhammad Abdullah ibn Yusuf al-Juwayni say: I saw Ibrahim al-Khalil, peace be upon him, in a dream. I bent down to kiss his feet, but he prevented me out of generosity to me. So I turned around and kissed his heels. I interpreted that elevation and blessing would remain in my heels. Then I said: O Friend of Allah, what do you say about the science of kalam? He said: 'By it are repelled doubts and falsehoods.' The Imam Abu Nasr Abd al-Rahim ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Hawazin informed us by permission, saying: My father, the master Abu al-Qasim al-Qushayri, may Allah have mercy on him, was asked: 'Do the people of tawhid differ in it?' He said: 'If you distinguish between two who pray, and you know that this one prays with his heart full of distractions, and that one prays with his heart present, then there is a difference between a scholar and a scholar. This one, if a problem occurs to him, he cannot extricate himself from it; that one resists every enemy of Islam and solves every difficult problem that is rare in the arena of disputation. And this is the greater jihad. For the outward jihad is against specific groups, but this is jihad against all enemies of religion.'
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage contains two reports. First, a dream narrated by al-Juwayni in which he sees Prophet Ibrahim (AS) and asks about kalam. Ibrahim responds that kalam repels doubts and falsehoods (shubah wa abatil). This serves as prophetic endorsement of the science. Second, al-Qushayri answers a question about whether people of tawhid differ in their level. He uses an analogy: two people praying, one heedless, one present; there is a difference between a scholar (alim) and a scholar. The true scholar of kalam can resolve any problem and resist all enemies of Islam in debate. This is described as the greater jihad because physical jihad is against specific enemies, but kalamic jihad is against all enemies of the religion (i.e., intellectual opponents).

Key Terms
علم الكلام (science of kalam)
الشبه والأباطيل (doubts and falsehoods)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That kalam is a bid'ah with no prophetic precedent.
Correction: Prophet Ibrahim's dream shows that kalam is a tool endorsed by a prophet to repel falsehood.

Checkpoint
What did Prophet Ibrahim say about kalam in the dream?
A) It is a bid'ah.
B) It repels doubts and falsehoods.
C) Only scholars should study it.
D) It is the same as tasawwuf.

Key Takeaway
Prophet Ibrahim endorsed kalam as the means to repel doubts and falsehoods, showing its prophetic roots.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to love Prophet Ibrahim as a model of faith. Yet when doubts about your religion arise, do you actually take up the weapon he endorsed? Or do you stay silent and let falsehoods creep in? What will you do today to begin actively defending the truth?
?
If you have ever dismissed theological study as unnecessary or divisive, how will you now change your attitude toward learning 'ilm al-kalam? Name one concrete step you will take this week to equip yourself against doubts.
?
The dream of al-Juwayni shows that even a prophet commands us to repel falsehoods. When you hear someone attacking Islam with modern arguments, do you feel prepared to respond? If not, what is holding you back from seeking that knowledge? This week, what will you learn about kalam?
